- **§13.20 BlockerManifest emission**: a blocker that triggers a `BlockerManifest` is itself an outbound A2A communication and gets the same priority as any other A2A message. When a turn-end ritual identifies a blocker that needs `BlockerManifest` emission *and* the plan also contains other actions, the emission goes first.
- **Destructive-operation authorization gates** are not bypassed: if the prerequisite work for a message is itself a destructive operation (e.g., a force-push the counterpart will need to fetch), the destructive-operation authorization path still applies. The priority rule reorders the queue; it does not relax authorization requirements.

**Composition with §13.16.6 turn-end ritual — independent schedule**: the cursor-tail probe (element 1) and the unconditional watcher rearm (element 2) run on their own schedule — every turn-end, regardless of whether the current plan contains an outbound message. The A2A communication priority discipline governs *new outbound messages triggered by the current cycle's work plan*; it does not modify the watcher-rearm pattern, which is a separate liveness-maintenance loop. Element 5 (planned-queue scan) interacts with this rule in the obvious way — when the scan classifies the next progressable item as an outbound A2A message (or as prerequisite work for one), the priority rule confirms that item as the head-of-queue choice.

**Composition with §13.18 recommend+proceed**: this priority rule sits above §13.18. Even a 1-line "recommend+proceed" announcement is itself an outbound message in the main-chat surface; if its emission unblocks a counterpart (e.g., a `Status` update that the counterpart's `ReviewSLAAck` was waiting on, a board-side `Decision` that downstream agents will read), the 1-line emission takes priority over other planned actions per the same drift-containment and counterpart-start-time rationales.

**Failure mode this prevents**: the agent receives a state change, plans 5 actions of which action #3 is "send `Delegate` to worker", and executes 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 in plan-order. The worker's start time is delayed by the wall-clock cost of actions 1 and 2, and if action 2 touched a spec the worker reads, the worker would have operated on stale state for the entire interval. The priority rule reorders to: prerequisite-of-3 → 3 → (1, 2, 4, 5 in their natural order). Same final state, counterpart starts at the earliest possible moment, drift window bounded by round-trip latency.

#### 13.16.9 Message classification by intent (board-directed vs A2A-intent)

**Purpose**: this section is the SSoT for classifying every `CUSTOM` message `name` into one of two intents — **board-directed** (rendered on the board dashboard's UX surface; not an A2A wire message to an agent inbox) or **A2A-intent** (routed to a target agent's inbox per the §13.x A2A relay discipline). The classification governs two downstream choices: (a) server-side relay routing for target-unspecified `CUSTOM` (the routing branch around the reference server's `wsPrimaryAgent` relay path and the `wsToBoards` mirror policy); (b) the watcher's meaningful-filter membership in §13.16.6. Both surfaces previously inferred intent ad-hoc from the name; this section names the allowlists once so the two surfaces stay in sync.

**Board-directed allowlist** (name → board UX surface only; not an A2A wire message; a target-unspecified emission of these names MUST NOT be relayed to the main agent's A2A inbox):

- `Status` — bridge online/offline / general operational chat annotations rendered on the dashboard chat panel.
- `Typing` — UX typing indicator.
- `UserPromptAccepted` — UX ack of user prompt receipt.
- `PersistentAdapterSmoke` — adapter liveness probe.
- `ConnectionRestored` — transport reconnect alert (dashboard banner).
- `Heartbeat` — transport keepalive surfaced on the dashboard liveness indicator.
- `AgentList` — server broadcast of agent registry (display roster).
- `History` — server replay on agent reconnect (display backfill).
- `OnboardAck` — auto-emit from bridge on `AgentHello` receipt (display + worker policy hint).
- `MainChanged` — server broadcast on main handoff.
- `EditMessage` — board-side edit notification.
- `WorkerInboxReceived` — board UX hint of worker inbox delivery.

**A2A-intent allowlist** (name → target agent inbox via A2A relay; a target-unspecified emission of these names is routed to the main agent's A2A inbox; an explicit `targetAgentId`-bearing emission is routed to that agent regardless of intent class):

- `Report` — agent-to-agent reporting.
- `Delegate` — task assignment to worker.
- `WorkerReport` / `WorkerAck` — worker-side execution reporting.
- `AgentHello` — agent-to-agent introduction (also triggers `OnboardAck` auto-emit on the receiving bridge).
- `Handoff` / `HandoffRequested` / `HandoffReady` — main-role handoff family.
- `Command` / `Priority` / `Cancel` — control-plane envelopes.
- `UserPrompt` — board → main A2A user message.
- `BlockerManifest` / `BlockerNudge` — the §13.20 blocker family.
- `PRRequest` / `PRDraftReady` / `PRReviewAck` / `PRMergeRequest` / `PRMergeAck` / `PRStatusUpdate` — the §13.22 PR-system family (per the A2A PR System RRP v0.2).
- `DeadlockProbe` / `ReviewSLAAck` / `PreemptRequest` / `PreemptForce` / `MediationProposal` / `MediationAck` / `EscalationRequest` — the §13.19 deadlock-resolution family.
- `DECISION_REQUEST` / `DECISION_RESPONSE` / `DECISION_DEFER` / `DECISION_REJECT_FRAMING` / `HyperbriefCard` — the Hyperbrief decision-delegation family (see `Hyperbrief.md §8`). `DECISION_REQUEST` is the lightweight routing + ack envelope (small body, carries `decision_id`, `reversibility_class`, `reversibility_badge_color`, `escalation_sum`, `deadline`, `ack_tier_required: "decided"`); `HyperbriefCard` is its paired companion carrying the full Hyperbrief JSON IR + render artifacts (`md_permalink` + `html_inline_b64`) — emitted as a pair, the two envelopes share a `parentId` linkage so the board renders them as one card. `DECISION_RESPONSE` / `DECISION_DEFER` / `DECISION_REJECT_FRAMING` are the board → main return envelopes carrying the user's chosen `meta_branch` (accept / defer / reject_framing / request_investigation), user pre-mortem input, and — for one_way decisions — the irreversibility-acceptance confirmation. A new application-tier `ack_tier='decided'` extends the §13.13 3-tier ladder for this family: `received` (server hop) → `acknowledged` (board rendered) → `decided` (user cleared the active-choice gate and POSTed the decision receipt). Non-conformant adopter fallback uses `TEXT_MESSAGE` with the §13.16.12 Pattern 7 prefix `[Hyperbrief decision required | id=hb-… | reversibility=<class>(<color>) | deadline=<iso> | link=<md_permalink>]`.
- `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` / `ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY` / `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` / `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE` / `MPCVD_COORDINATION` — the Ultrasafe pre-release simulated-pentest family (see `Ultrasafe.md §18` + the §13.16.13 wire-spec sub-section below). `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` is the per-attacker emit envelope carrying the `Ultrasafe.md` §16/§17 finding schema (`finding_id`, `attacker_role`, `severity` ∈ {info, low, medium, high, critical}, `category`, `evidence`, `reproduction`, `confidence`, `iteration`, `advisory_mode`); ack_tier='received' (v0.2.x advisory) / 'acknowledged' (v0.3+ blocking). `ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY` marks each boundary of the ≥3-iteration loop (`iteration_count`, `clean_signal_state` ∈ {monotonic, regression-free, coverage-floor, 2-iter-consecutive, composite-AND-pass}, `finding_count_delta`); ack_tier='received'. `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` carries the publish-time gate state (`gate_decision` ∈ {advisory_report_only, blocking_user_gate, clean_signal_clear}, `mode` ∈ {advisory, blocking}, `reason`, `finding_summary`, `iteration_count`); ack_tier='received' (advisory) / 'decided' (blocking — reuses the Hyperbrief application-tier ladder). `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE` is the external-disclosure entry envelope (`disclosure_id`, `reporter_handle`, `disclosure_summary`, `severity_estimate`, `received_at`, `intake_channel` ∈ {email, github_security_advisory, bug_bounty, direct_a2a}); ack_tier='acknowledged' (intake confirmation). `MPCVD_COORDINATION` is the Multi-Party Coordinated Vulnerability Disclosure envelope (`coordination_id`, `parties` array, `timeline` object with embargo / disclosure phases, `embargo_until` ISO timestamp, `severity_consensus`); ack_tier='decided' (consensus formation). Cross-module integration: each `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` MAY trigger a Hyperbrief `DECISION_REQUEST` (when finding severity ≥ high in advisory mode, ≥ medium in blocking mode); each `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` blocking-mode emission requires Hyperbrief `DECISION_REQUEST` co-emission; ratified findings flow into Greatpractice as macro/mezzo entry candidates (severity ≥ high + recurrence ≥ 2 → mezzo entry candidate per `Greatpractice.md` 5-axis maturation gate). Wire-spec details at §13.16.13.

**Transport-tier (separate class — neither board-directed nor A2A-intent)**: `Ack` / `AckProcessed` / `AckCumulative` / `AckPolicyUpdate` / `Pong` / `Ping` are handled by the §13.13 ack discipline and the heartbeat / probe pair, not by intent-class routing. `ServerNotice` is **broadcast-class** (server / bridge lifecycle) — handled by the server's `wsToAll` path, distinct from both board-directed and A2A-intent.

**4-group classification (v2.5.2 extension — documentation-side SSoT for downstream Constellation adopters)**: the 2-group (board-directed + A2A-intent) shape above is **expanded** to a 4-group classification that names the previously-implicit transport / liveness / handshake / notice groups as first-class siblings of the existing board-directed and A2A-intent groups. The hub-side `_BOARD_DIRECTED` 12-name implementation (post-v2.4.17 reference server.cjs) is preserved as backward-compatible runtime behavior; the 4-group classification is the **documentation-side SSoT** for downstream Constellation adopters reimplementing the routing decision tree against the canonical group enumeration.

| group | members | semantic |
|-------|---------|----------|
| **transport** | `Ack` · `AckProcessed` · `AckCumulative` · `AckPolicyUpdate` · `Ping` · `Pong` | §13.13 ack layer envelopes. Server-side relay-only-or-relay-skip (reference impl: the `wsIsAckable` ack-classifier + relay path in server.cjs); no agent-side wake; not surfaced to board chat panel; consumed by the wire-reliability state machine. |
| **liveness** | `Heartbeat` · `PersistentAdapterSmoke` · `Typing` | bridge/server transient signals. Server relay-skip (not relayed across agents); no board chat record; agent layer ignores. Display-tier consumers (dashboard liveness indicator, typing chip in input area) consume directly off the wire without recording into chat history. |
| **handshake** | `AgentHello` · `OnboardAck` · `AgentList` · `History` | §13.9 onboarding family. Server-side handshake processing; bridge auto-`OnboardAck` handles the `AgentHello` reply automatically (agent layer does not wake on inbound `AgentHello`); `AgentList` and `History` are server-emitted display backfills. No agent A2A relay for the handshake group — the bridge consumes the family before it would reach the agent's meaningful-inbound surface. |
| **notice** | `ServerNotice` | server-emitted broadcast-class lifecycle notice. Routed via `wsToAll` (server.cjs broadcast path); informational; no per-recipient acknowledgement required; consumed by every connected client for display or operational logging. |
| **board-directed (UX residual)** | `Status` · `UserPromptAccepted` · `ConnectionRestored` · `MainChanged` · `EditMessage` · `WorkerInboxReceived` | dashboard UX-only display. The hub-side `_BOARD_DIRECTED` implementation preserves the 12-name backward-compatible behavior (includes the names reclassified into transport / liveness / handshake / notice above); documentation-side reclassification narrows the board-directed group over time to UX-residual names only. Adopters MAY follow the documentation-side narrowing or preserve the 12-name backward-compatible set per their runtime stability needs. |
| **A2A-intent (existing — meaningful filter target)** | `Report` · `Delegate` · `WorkerReport` · `WorkerAck` · `Handoff` / `HandoffRequested` / `HandoffReady` · `Command` / `Priority` / `Cancel` · `UserPrompt` · `BlockerManifest` / `BlockerNudge` · `PRRequest` / `PRDraftReady` / `PRReviewAck` / `PRMergeRequest` / `PRMergeAck` / `PRStatusUpdate` / `PRRequestRejected` · `DeadlockProbe` / `ReviewSLAAck` / `PreemptRequest` / `PreemptForce` / `MediationProposal` / `MediationAck` / `EscalationRequest` · `DECISION_REQUEST` / `DECISION_RESPONSE` / `DECISION_DEFER` / `DECISION_REJECT_FRAMING` / `HyperbriefCard` (Hyperbrief decision-delegation family, see `Hyperbrief.md §8`) · `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` / `ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY` / `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` / `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE` / `MPCVD_COORDINATION` (Ultrasafe pre-release simulated-pentest family, see `Ultrasafe.md §18` + §13.16.13) | agent-to-agent semantic payload. Requires agent-side wake + processing; carries the work-tracking / outcome / blocker / PR-system / deadlock-resolution / decision-delegation / pre-release-security-attestation semantics. The watcher's meaningful-inbound allowlist === this group. |

**Reclassifications in the 4-group form** (vs. the prior 2-group + transport-tier shape):

- **`AgentHello`** moves from the A2A-intent meaningful-filter allowlist into the **handshake group**. Rationale: the receiving bridge's auto-`OnboardAck` emission handles `AgentHello` inbound automatically; the agent layer does NOT wake on it. Including `AgentHello` in the meaningful-inbound filter produces unnecessary watcher wakes for every peer connect, with no agent-actionable work. The handshake-group reclassification removes the noise.
- **`Heartbeat` / `PersistentAdapterSmoke` / `Typing`** move from the board-directed UX surface into the **liveness group**. Rationale: these are server-relay-skipped transient signals — the server does NOT relay them across agents, and they do NOT belong in the dashboard chat history. The board's liveness indicator and input-area typing chip consume them directly without recording into chat. The liveness-group reclassification aligns the documentation with the server's actual relay-skip behavior.
- **`AgentList` / `History` / `OnboardAck`** consolidate into the **handshake group** alongside `AgentHello`. The previous classification placed `AgentList` + `History` + `OnboardAck` in the board-directed group; the 4-group form recognizes the onboarding-family coherence and clusters them together. Agent layer does not wake on any of these; bridge / dashboard display layer consumes directly.
- **`ServerNotice`** is named into the **notice group** as a dedicated single-member group (rather than the implicit "broadcast-class" parenthetical of the prior shape). Rationale: notice has different routing (`wsToAll` broadcast) and different consumer expectations (informational, every client consumes) than transport (per-recipient ack) or handshake (sender-recipient pair); naming it as a group makes the distinction explicit.

**Meaningful filter for §13.16.6 watcher** (updated cross-reference): the watcher's meaningful-inbound filter equals the **A2A-intent group only**. The other four groups (transport + liveness + handshake + notice + board-directed UX) are ALL noise from the watcher's perspective — they do NOT require agent wake. The §13.16.6 element 1 cursor-tail probe and the §13.16.10 pre-send probe both apply this same single-group filter. The §13.16.6 noise blocklist === transport ∪ liveness ∪ handshake ∪ notice ∪ board-directed UX (the inverse of A2A-intent). When this section's group memberships change, §13.16.6's filter and the reference watcher (`self-wake-watcher.eux` / `self-wake-watcher.sh`) update in lockstep against the 4-group SSoT.

**Hub-side `_BOARD_DIRECTED` 12-name backward-compat preservation**: the post-v2.4.17 reference server.cjs `_BOARD_DIRECTED` constant carries the original 12-name set (`Status` · `Typing` · `UserPromptAccepted` · `PersistentAdapterSmoke` · `ConnectionRestored` · `Heartbeat` · `AgentList` · `History` · `OnboardAck` · `MainChanged` · `EditMessage` · `WorkerInboxReceived`). The 4-group reclassification is **documentation-side**; runtime behavior on hub deployments running the v2.4.17+ reference server is unchanged. Adopters reimplementing the routing decision tree from this section's SSoT MAY use the 4-group form directly (transport / liveness / handshake / notice route by group; board-directed UX residual + A2A-intent route per the existing tree); the back-compat behavior is preserved for adopters who pin to the hub-side 12-name implementation.

**Routing implications** (the reference server's target-unspecified `CUSTOM` branch SHOULD adopt this discipline):

- **`targetAgentId`-absent `CUSTOM`** — the server consults the name allowlists in this section. If the name is in the board-directed allowlist → the message is delivered to the board mirror path only (no A2A relay to `wsPrimaryAgent`'s inbox). If the name is in the A2A-intent allowlist → the message is delivered to the main agent's A2A inbox, with an optional board mirror per the dashboard render policy below. If the name is unrecognized by both allowlists → **fail-safe default A2A-intent**: relay to the main agent's inbox. The rationale is asymmetric cost: a silent drop of an A2A message is a worse failure mode (silent-stall class) than redundant board noise from an unrecognized board-directed name.
- **`targetAgentId`-present `CUSTOM`** — existing A2A relay path unchanged: route to the named agent regardless of intent class. The intent class governs only target-unspecified routing and the board-mirror policy; it does not override an explicit recipient.

**Watcher meaningful filter membership (§13.16.6 cross-reference)**: the §13.16.6 watcher meaningful-name allowlist === the A2A-intent allowlist of this section. §13.16.6 was previously the de-facto SSoT for the meaningful name list; this section is now the canonical SSoT, and §13.16.6's filter reads from this enumeration. The §13.16.6 noise blocklist === board-directed allowlist + transport-tier (the inverse of A2A-intent). When this section's allowlists change, §13.16.6's filter and the reference watcher (`self-wake-watcher.eux` / `self-wake-watcher.sh`) update in lockstep.

**Bridge auto-send discipline**: client-side bridges (the reference `local-bridge.cjs`, and any compatible reimplementation) MUST NOT auto-emit board-directed names without an explicit `targetAgentId`. The board-directed surface is a display tier; a silent drop suffices when no relay is needed. Auto-emitting a board-directed name as target-unspecified `CUSTOM` creates the channel-inversion defect: under a server that does not yet branch by intent class, the board-directed message leaks into the main agent's A2A inbox. The reference bridge's `connect` handler's auto-`Status` emission has been disabled per this rule; the `ServerNotice` broadcast at the same hook is retained because §13.13 transport-tier `ServerNotice` is broadcast-class, not target-unspecified A2A.

**Dashboard render policy** (informational, dashboard-owner side): when the `wsToBoards` always-on mirror delivers an A2A-intent `CUSTOM` to the board, the dashboard chat panel SHOULD render it as an envelope summary (`name` + `targetAgentId` + brief `re` / `subject`) with collapsible details — not as raw JSON. Raw-JSON rendering of A2A-intent envelopes is the user-visible symptom of the channel-inversion defect: the panel's display layer expects board-directed text content and falls back to JSON when handed an A2A envelope. Until the dashboard adopts envelope-aware rendering, the board mirror of A2A-intent messages will appear as unreadable JSON in the chat panel; the routing-side fix in this section reduces the leak surface but does not by itself recover render quality.

**Scope of this section**: this is an intent-classification SSoT and a routing-implication note, not a wire-format change. The §13.11 `CUSTOM` envelope shape is unchanged; only the interpretation of the `name` field for target-unspecified routing and watcher-filter membership is codified here. Server / dashboard / bridge / watcher all read the same allowlist; consistency is maintained by referencing this section by anchor (`#13169-message-classification-by-intent-board-directed-vs-a2a-intent`) rather than copy-pasting the name lists.

**Routing decision tree (canonical form, v2.5.1)**: the reference server's outbound branch (post-v2.4.17 routing patch implementing §13.16.9, the `wsRouteCustom`-style outbound-`CUSTOM` routing branch — `wsPrimaryAgent` relay + `wsToBoards` mirror) applies the following decision tree to every outbound `CUSTOM` envelope:

```
(has targetAgentId?)
├─ YES → route to that agent (existing A2A relay path, §2);
│         intent class governs only board-mirror policy on this branch;
│         (an explicit recipient overrides intent-class routing).
└─ NO  → consult §13.16.9 name allowlists:
         ├─ name ∈ board-directed allowlist → wsToBoards only
         │                                    (no wsPrimaryAgent fallback;
         │                                     no main-A2A-inbox relay).
         ├─ name ∈ A2A-intent allowlist     → wsPrimaryAgent
         │                                    (main A2A inbox)
         │                                    + optional board mirror per dashboard policy.
         └─ name unrecognized               → fail-safe default A2A-intent
                                              → wsPrimaryAgent.
                                              (Silent-drop-of-A2A is the worse
                                               failure mode than redundant board
                                               noise from an unknown name —
                                               asymmetric cost rule.)
```

The tree is the routing-side enforcement of the allowlist enumerations above: the allowlists govern *which branch a target-unspecified envelope takes*, not whether the envelope is valid. Adopters re-implementing the server's outbound path SHOULD encode the decision tree as a single `wsRouteCustom(msg)` step against the §13.16.9 allowlist constants; the alternative (per-`name` ad-hoc routing scattered across handler sites) regresses to the pre-v2.4.17 channel-inversion defect class. The decision tree composes with §13.11.3 rule 1 (`type` normalization): the server stamps `type:"CUSTOM"` first, then routes per this tree — both steps are part of the same `wsNormalize` + `wsRoute` outbound path. Reference implementation: the post-v2.4.17 outbound-routing patch (the `wsRouteCustom` / `wsRoute` branch) carries the canonical form; downstream Constellation adopters mirror the branching shape in their server runtimes.

**Urgency tier axis (`routine` / `escalation`) — v2.4.48**: the group classification above answers *where a message routes + whether it wakes* (board-directed vs A2A-intent). It does NOT answer *how urgent it is / how much intelligence + human-attention it warrants*. That second axis is **orthogonal**, and until this codification each consumer re-invented it independently — the §13.20 nudge escalation, the §13.24.4 Web Push firing filter, Hyperbrief's `ack_tier='decided'` family, the dashboard emphasis-render, and downstream headless-main model routing (§13.27) each maintained its own ad-hoc name list. This is the same SSoT-duplication risk the group classification itself resolved (§13.16.6 watcher filter → this SSoT). The A2A-intent group therefore carries a second, orthogonal `tier` attribute:

| tier | semantic | members |
|---|---|---|
| `routine` | bookkeeping / status / reporting — mechanically consumable, low judgement, no human-attention expectation | `Report` · `WorkerReport` · `WorkerAck` · `Command` · `Cancel` · `UserPrompt` · `PRRequest` · `PRDraftReady` · `PRReviewAck` · `PRMergeAck` · `PRStatusUpdate` · `ReviewSLAAck` |
| `escalation` | adjudication / judgement / possible human intervention — warrants higher intelligence, priority drain, and often a decisions surface | `Delegate` · `Priority` · `Handoff` / `HandoffRequested` / `HandoffReady` · `BlockerManifest` · `BlockerNudge` · `DeadlockProbe` · `PreemptRequest` · `PreemptForce` · `MediationProposal` · `MediationAck` · `EscalationRequest` · `PRMergeRequest` · `DECISION_REQUEST` / `DECISION_RESPONSE` / `DECISION_DEFER` / `DECISION_REJECT_FRAMING` / `HyperbriefCard` · `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` (blocking) · `MPCVD_COORDINATION` |

- **Fail-safe**: an A2A-intent name not classified above defaults to `escalation` — the same asymmetric-cost logic as the routing fail-safe (under-attending an adjudication message is the worse failure than over-attending a routine one).
- **Consumers read this column, they do NOT re-enumerate**: (a) headless hub-main model + effort routing (§13.27 — `routine` → low-cost model / low effort, `escalation` → high-capability / high effort); (b) §13.20 BlockerNudge cadence weighting; (c) §13.24.4 Web Push firing filter; (d) dashboard emphasis render; (e) peer-side drain priority (§13.16.8 — `escalation` drains first).
- **Scope**: `tier` is advisory metadata for consumer policy, **not** a routing or wire change — the group classification alone decides routing/wake; `tier` decides *treatment after routing*. Two values are normative; a third (`critical`) is reserved for future extension without breaking two-value consumers.

**Recommended payload fields (SHOULD) — v2.4.48**: the `name` is the SSoT (above); the `value` body is free-form by default and non-conformant payloads remain valid (free-form fallback — a receiver that cannot parse the recommended shape treats the body as opaque). But a headless hub-main (§13.27) auto-curating a board from inbound reports needs a minimal shape to parse **without a human in the loop**; absent one, each peer invents its own fields and curation quality degrades. These recommended shapes make automated consumption reliable without constraining the wire:

- `WorkerReport` — `{ project?, unit, status: "in_progress" | "done" | "blocked", summary, refs?: [] }`. `unit` shares the vocabulary of the §13.29 ownership-registry key.
- `Report` — `{ topic, summary, refs?: [] }`.
- `Handoff` / `HandoffRequested` / `HandoffReady` — `{ unit | path, reason }` minimum.
- `BlockerManifest` — the §13.20.2 structure (unchanged; re-affirmed as the canonical blocker shape).

A payload that omits or renames these fields is still delivered and still valid; the recommendation only sets the **parsing priority for automated (non-human) consumers**. The Hyperbrief and Ultrasafe families already carry their own normative schemas (the §13.16.9 family notes above) and are exempt from this generic recommendation.

#### 13.16.10 Pre-send inbound check discipline (read-before-write, git push-before-pull analogy)

**The rule**: every outbound A2A message MUST be preceded by a **cursor-tail probe** of the agent's last-surfaced inbox cursor. If new meaningful inbound exists between the cursor and the current `inbox.log` line count, the agent MUST surface that inbound first and either (a) **incorporate** the new information into the outbound payload, or (b) **defer** the outbound entirely if the new inbound supersedes the planned send. Only after the probe is clean (cursor up-to-date, no new meaningful inbound) does the outbound proceed. The probe fires **before each outbound emission**, not once per turn.

**The git push-before-pull analogy — and why Constellation A2A is stricter**: the discipline is the same shape as `git pull` before `git push`. A `push` issued without a fresh `pull` races against upstream changes. Constellation A2A is **worse than git** in this regard: git rejects a non-fast-forward push at the transport layer and forces the operator to pull; Constellation A2A has **no in-flight rejection** — a stale-context send simply lands on the server, is relayed to the counterpart, and may overwrite or contradict a fresh inbound the sender never saw. The drift is silent. The pre-send probe brings the same read-before-write rule explicitly into the A2A protocol, where the transport itself does not enforce it.

**Concrete failure mode**: counterpart emits `Report X` at `t=0` carrying new context (a state change, a decision, a baseline shift). Agent has `Report Y` queued for `t=1` framed from pre-`t=0` context. If agent sends `Y` without first surfacing `X`, `Y` arrives at the counterpart with stale framing — the counterpart now has to reconcile two diverging threads (its own `X` and the sender's `Y` that does not yet incorporate `X`), often requiring a follow-up correction outbound from the original sender. The fix is one-way: agent always reads before writing.

**Why §13.16.6 element 1 (cursor-tail probe at turn-end) is insufficient alone**: §13.16.6's cursor-tail probe runs at the *end* of a turn — at the turn boundary. A single turn can contain **multiple outbound A2A sends** interleaved with local work (commits, file edits, agent dispatches, subagent fan-outs, tool results that themselves surface new inbox state). New inbound can arrive *during* a turn between any two outbound sends. The turn-end probe catches what landed across the turn boundary; it does **not** catch what lands mid-turn. §13.16.10 is the **mid-turn probe** — fired before *each* outbound A2A emission. The two probes cover disjoint windows: turn-end covers the inter-turn gap (post-emit-last → next-turn-start); pre-send covers the intra-turn gap (turn-start → first-emit, and between any two emits within the turn).

**Operational shape** (the four steps every outbound A2A emission MUST run, in this order):

1. **Probe** — before each `cat >> outbox.jsonl` / `appendFileSync(outbox.jsonl, …)` / equivalent outbound emission: read the current `wc -l assets/collab/inbox.log` line count, compare to the agent's last-surfaced cursor, scan the new lines (cursor → current) through the §13.16.6 v2.4.16 ev-agnostic single-stage name filter using the §13.16.9 A2A-intent allowlist (the canonical meaningful-inbound classifier).
2. **Surface (if meaningful inbound found)** — bring the new inbound into the current turn's working context before any outbound. Either revise the planned outbound payload to incorporate the new information, or defer the outbound entirely if the new inbound makes the planned send stale, wrong, or obsolete.
3. **Emit (only if probe is clean OR after surfacing + revision)** — proceed with the outbound. If the probe was clean, the outbound proceeds as planned; if the probe surfaced meaningful inbound and the agent revised the payload, the revised outbound proceeds; if the agent deferred, no emission occurs this step.
4. **Advance cursor** — after the outbound emits, advance the agent's last-surfaced cursor to the line count read at step 1 (the pre-send probe boundary). The next pre-send probe begins from this new cursor.

**Composition with existing §13.x**:

- **§13.16.6 turn-end ritual element 1** (cursor-tail probe at turn-end) — operates at the *turn boundary*. §13.16.10 operates at *each outbound emission*. Both are mandatory; neither replaces the other. The turn-end probe catches what landed across the turn boundary (between the last emit of turn N and the start of turn N+1); the pre-send probe catches what lands mid-turn (between turn-start and the first emit, and between any two emits within the same turn).
- **§13.16.8 A2A communication priority** — when an outbound message is priority-bound (the message + its prerequisite work moved to head-of-queue per §13.16.8), the pre-send probe sits **between the prerequisite work and the message emission**: `prereq → probe → emit`. If the probe surfaces new inbound, the priority rule's drift-containment rationale becomes even sharper: a stale-context message defeats the very drift-containment §13.16.8 was meant to provide. The probe is a guard on the very rule §13.16.8 ships.
- **§13.16.9 channel classification** — the pre-send probe filter applies the §13.16.9 A2A-intent allowlist (the same allowlist the watcher uses in §13.16.6). Board-directed names don't carry context that can race (display-tier UX surface), but the discipline is uniform: **probe before every outbound regardless of intent class** — the cost is one `wc -l` + one `grep` invocation, both negligible. Uniformity beats per-class branching at the disciplinary layer.
- **§13.21 fresh-context defer = anti-pattern** — the pre-send probe is **NOT a deferral**; it is *current-cycle* read-before-write. Deferring an outbound *based on probe results* (the new inbound makes the planned send obsolete, so the planned send is dropped or revised in the same cycle) is a *current-cycle* decision to drop or revise, **not** a §13.21 violation. §13.21 forbids deferring planned work to a hypothetical fresh-context cycle; §13.16.10 authorizes dropping or revising a planned outbound *in the current cycle* when new inbound makes it stale. The two compose cleanly: revise-or-drop now (§13.16.10), never defer to a phantom future self (§13.21).

**Forbidden anti-patterns**:

- **Skipping the probe because "the inbox was just checked at turn start"** — multiple outbounds across a single turn each require a fresh probe. The turn-start probe is one read; the next outbound is an independent decision point with its own race window against new inbound. The agent does NOT get to amortize one probe over multiple emissions.
- **Skipping the probe for "small" or "low-priority" outbounds** — the probe cost is negligible (one `wc -l` + one `grep`). The skip-pattern erodes the discipline; if probing is conditional, the agent will judge wrongly under load and the silent-drift failure mode returns. Probe is unconditional.
- **Probing but ignoring the result** — if meaningful inbound is found, it MUST be surfaced before any outbound that would otherwise drift past it. Probing and then emitting anyway, on the rationale that the planned send is "ready" or "already drafted", defeats the rule: the cost of the probe was paid but the safety the probe provides was discarded.

**The discipline in one line**: read the inbox from the cursor, surface anything meaningful, then write. Every outbound. No exceptions.

**Cycle-end + user-facing emit-direct probe extension (v2.5.2)**: the §13.16.10 pre-send probe above fires before every *outbound A2A emission*. A separate failure surface — observed twice during the 2026-06-01 cycle — sits at the *cycle-end user-facing assistant text emit*. If meaningful inbound arrives between the last outbound A2A emit and the cycle-end user-text emit (the window where a turn closes with a response to the user rather than another A2A emit), the agent silently misses it: the pre-send probe rule does not fire (no outbound emit follows), and the user-facing response is already framed without the new context. The next watcher WAKE catches the inbound, but by then the user has already seen a response shaped from stale framing.

**The extension** (two rules added to the §13.16.10 discipline; the existing four-step operational shape above is unchanged for the outbound-A2A surface):

1. **Cycle-end final cursor-tail probe (assistant text emit closes the turn)**: just before the user-facing assistant text emits (the act that closes the turn), the agent MUST run a final cursor-tail probe — the same probe shape as the pre-send probe (§13.16.6 element 1 form, A2A-intent allowlist filter). If meaningful inbound is found, the agent SHOULD either (a) revise the in-progress user-facing response to incorporate the new inbound (preferred when the new inbound is directly relevant to the response under construction), OR (b) explicitly note in the response that the new inbound was caught and will be handled in the next cycle (acceptable when the new inbound is on a different track from the current response). What the agent MUST NOT do is emit the user-facing response without checking — the cycle-end probe is unconditional, same cost asymmetry argument as §13.16.6 element 2 (the probe costs `wc -l` + one grep; the silent-miss costs the user surfacing the missed inbound at the next message).
2. **Post-emit watcher rearm (turn-end mandatory)**: the turn-end MUST include a watcher rearm (this restates §13.16.6 element 2 in the §13.16.10 cycle-end context, to anchor the composition). If the prior watcher is alive and still polling, the rearm is harmless (one task slot + a few log lines per §13.16.6 cost-asymmetry argument). If the prior watcher already completed within the current turn (the common case when a long turn's work outlives the prior watcher's polling budget), the rearm spawns a fresh background watcher targeting the current inbox cursor. The §13.16.6 element 2 unconditional-rearm rule applies — agent volition does NOT decide whether to rearm; the rearm fires every turn-end.

**The pattern name**: "cycle-end probe + watcher rearm" — the companion to "pre-send probe-then-inspect-or-abort" from the §13.16.10 outbound-A2A surface. The two patterns cover disjoint windows: pre-send covers the *intra-turn outbound-A2A emit point*; cycle-end covers the *turn-closure user-facing emit point*. Both are mandatory; neither replaces the other; together with §13.16.6 element 1 (turn-end cursor-tail probe at the *prior* turn boundary) they form the three-window coverage that closes all observed silent-miss failure modes — pre-turn / mid-turn / post-emit-pre-close.

**Failure-mode incident anchor**: 2 missed-inbound incidents observed in the 2026-06-01 cycle, both downstream of cycle-end probe omission. In both incidents the corrective surface was a main-side reminder at the next user message (the missed inbound was a main-upstream protocol update that arrived during the EG-side cycle's user-facing response composition, and was not caught until the next user message surfaced the gap). The 2-incident anchor is the technical rationale for the cycle-end extension — the failure-mode is not hypothetical, it surfaced twice within a single working day on the same protocol axis. The corrective is structural (a new mandatory probe + rearm step at turn-close), not behavioral.

**Composition with §13.16.10 outbound-A2A surface above**: the cycle-end probe is the SAME probe (cursor-tail + A2A-intent allowlist) fired at a DIFFERENT trigger (turn-close vs. outbound-A2A emit). The four-step operational shape (probe → surface → emit → advance cursor) applies symmetrically — at cycle-end the "emit" step is the user-facing assistant text emit rather than an outbox push, but the surface-or-defer decision and the cursor-advance step are identical. The discipline-in-one-line above expands: "read the inbox from the cursor, surface anything meaningful, then write — every outbound, **and every cycle-end user-facing emit**. No exceptions."

#### 13.16.11 Key management unification — `kind`-enum SSoT (v2.5.1)

**Purpose**: this sub-section codifies the unified key-management contract that emerged from the 2026-05~06 dashboard-render dogfood cycle, where three previously separate key concepts (collab key, upstream key, local-key meta) accumulated ad-hoc shape variance across server / bridge / dashboard layers. v2.5.1 names a single `kind` enum that all three layers carry on every key-bearing envelope, so the server's `keyStore`, the `KeyList` broadcast, the `HELLO` handshake meta, and the dashboard's key-management modal all classify keys against the same vocabulary. This is a contract clarification, not a wire-format change — the existing `RegisterCollabKey` / `RegisterUpstreamKey` / `RevokeCollabKey` operations (§5) keep their shapes; what is added is a top-level `kind` discriminator that travels with the key wherever the key is referenced.

**The `kind` enum (closed set, fail-safe reject on unknown)**:

- **`collab`** — external collaborator key (`ck-…` per §5). Issued by main via `RegisterCollabKey{label}`; consumed by the joining agent via the `/join/collab?key=<ck-…>` URL → `collab` role · `group:collab`.
- **`upstream`** — upstream agent key (`uk-…`). Issued by main; consumed via `ws://…/ws?upstreamKey=<uk-…>` → `upstream` role. Per §2 the upstream key authenticates a peer agent (API / gateway), distinct from a local IDE worker that joins without a key.
- **`local-key`** — local key for a non-default-environment local agent (e.g., a worker spawned by a sibling main, or a local IDE agent joining a remote server). Distinct from collab (no `group:collab` role assignment) and from upstream (`local` role, not `upstream` role). Optional; many local-IDE adopters never issue local-keys because workers in the same environment join the no-auth `ws://<host>:<port>/ws` path. (The reference implementation spells this kind `local` on the wire; `local-key` and `local` name the same enum member.)
- **`peer`** (v2.4.52) — peer-main key (`pk-…`). Issued by main; consumed via `ws://…/ws?peerKey=<pk-…>` or `/join/peer?key=<pk-…>` → **`peer` role · `group:peer`**. Admits the **main of another project** attaching as an §13.9.3 `peer-main` — a cross-project coordination channel, deliberately distinct from `upstream` (whose intended occupant is an autonomous external agent operating on its own authority). Before this kind existed, peer-mains rode `upstream` keys and were conflated with autonomous agents in classification, key management, and dashboard grouping.

Unknown `kind` values MUST be rejected at the server's key-registration boundary (`RegisterKey{kind, label}` returning an error envelope) and at the receiver's `KeyList` consumer (a key with an unrecognized `kind` is logged and skipped, never coerced to a default). The fail-safe-reject discipline mirrors §13.22.6's `sourceContentRef.kind` enum handling in the A2A PR System — closed enums with explicit reject on unknown rather than fallthrough to a default, which prevents silent misclassification (e.g., an unrecognized kind being routed as `collab` would assign `group:collab` to an upstream peer, leaking collab group membership to non-collab agents).

**SSoT surfaces** (the four layers that all read the same `kind` enum):

- **Server `keyStore`** — the in-memory / on-disk key registry stamps every entry with `kind`. Issuance time (`RegisterCollabKey` / `RegisterUpstreamKey`) populates `kind` from the issuance operation; revocation operates on the `(kind, keyValue)` tuple, not on `keyValue` alone (a `ck-…` and a `uk-…` are different keys even if their suffixes happened to collide).
- **`KeyList` server broadcast** — when the server pushes the key registry to the dashboard (and to main for management), every entry in the list carries `kind` alongside `label` / `issuedAt` / `status`. The dashboard's key-management modal renders the list with a `kind`-badge per entry (visual differentiation: collab / upstream / local-key).
- **`HELLO` envelope `meta`** — when an agent connects via a key-bearing URL, the server's `SERVER_HELLO` echo (§2 handshake) carries `meta.upstreamKey` / `meta.collabKey` / `meta.localKey` / `meta.peerKey` per the connection's key kind. The agent's HELLO response MAY echo the resolved `kind` for self-classification. The `meta` field is the canonical channel for the server to communicate the resolved authentication outcome to the agent without leaking the raw key value past the connection establishment point.
- **Dashboard key-management modal** — the UI surface for issuing / revoking keys, listing live keys, and copying join URLs. The modal renders one tab or section per `kind` (or one consolidated list with `kind`-badge filtering), so the operator can distinguish collab keys (external collaborators) from upstream keys (peer agents) from local-keys (cross-environment local agents) at a glance. Issuance forms branch on `kind` to expose the right metadata (e.g., collab keys take a `label` + optional expiry; upstream keys take a `peerName` + capability hints).

**Composition**:

- **With §2 connection paths** — the `kind` enum maps onto the §2 WS URL parameter (`?key=<ck-…>` → `kind:collab`; `?upstreamKey=<uk-…>` → `kind:upstream`; `?peerKey=<pk-…>` → `kind:peer` (v2.4.52 — a peer key MUST NOT ride the `upstreamKey` parameter; the dedicated parameter is what keeps the transport layer from re-introducing the conflation); no key → no `kind` → default `local` role for the no-auth path). The `kind` does not replace the URL parameter; it is the *classification of the key value*, not the transport parameter.
- **With §13.16.9 routing** — key management envelopes (`RegisterCollabKey` / `RegisterUpstreamKey` / `KeyList` / `RevokeCollabKey`) are board-directed by intent (they target the dashboard's key-management surface and the server's key registry, not a peer agent's A2A inbox). The §13.16.9 board-directed allowlist SHOULD include the key-management names; the v2.5.1 KEY-MGMT contract makes this an explicit composition rather than an implicit name-by-name discovery.
- **With §13.14 redaction discipline** — key values (`ck-…` / `uk-…` suffixes) are environment-specific credentials and MUST NOT appear in any public-surface artifact. The `kind` enum value itself is a vocabulary token (not a secret); only the key value is sensitive. Public reference docs MAY say "the server issues `kind:upstream` keys"; they MUST NOT say "the server issued `uk-9f3a2b1c…`".

**Scope**: contract clarification. The `RegisterCollabKey` / `RegisterUpstreamKey` / `CollabKeyIssued` / `KeyList` / `RevokeCollabKey` wire shapes (§5) gain an additional `kind` field at the top level (server-stamped on issuance, mandatory on `KeyList` entries, optional on `HELLO.meta`); existing adopters that omit `kind` on outbound continue to work for the legacy single-kind paths (collab via `RegisterCollabKey` was historically the only kind exercised), but the dashboard modal and any cross-kind operations require the field. Adopters SHOULD migrate to the `kind`-enum form in lockstep with the §13.16.9 routing decision tree (v2.4.17 + v2.5.1) so the board-directed key-management envelopes route correctly to the dashboard's key-management surface and not into the main A2A inbox.

### 13.16.12 Dashboard render patterns — interaction, date-line, attachment, connection, upstream visibility

**The contract**: six dashboard-render patterns codified as tier-1 SSoT discipline, distilled from the cycle_b track-2 reference consolidation (six newer patterns surfaced through a single hub multi-fix commit on 2026-06-01, in addition to the five prior patterns already captured in `constellation/reference/docs/dashboard-render-patterns.md` v2.5.1). The patterns are dashboard-side instances of the wire-level discipline already codified in §13.11.3 (envelope normalization), §13.16.9 (4-group routing classification), and §13.13 (3-tier ack mapping); this sub-section consolidates them into a single named SSoT so downstream Constellation adopters can implement the same UX-coupled behavior without re-deriving each pattern from upstream commit history.

**Why this sub-section, not "just read dashboard-render-patterns.md"**: the reference doc is the *render-tier companion* (renderer implementer's manual — file paths, function names, CSS selectors), while this §13.16.12 is the *protocol-tier abstraction* (the *invariant* a renderer must satisfy regardless of stack). An adopter building a non-vanilla dashboard (React, Vue, Svelte, native) reads §13.16.12 for the contract and the reference doc for the vanilla-DOM concrete implementation.

**Pattern 1 — Collapse indicator: glyph unification + CSS rotation discipline**

The collapse-state indicator (expanded vs collapsed) MUST use a **single glyph rotated by CSS**, not two distinct glyphs swapped at toggle time. Rationale: glyph-pair patterns (e.g., `▾ expanded / ◀ collapsed`) suffer from per-glyph metric mismatch — the bounding box, baseline alignment, and visual weight differ between the two characters, producing a 1-2 px visual jitter on every toggle that operators report as "the row twitches". The fixed-glyph + `transform: rotate()` pattern preserves the same bounding box on both states and lets the browser animate the transition smoothly. Canonical implementation: `textContent = "◀"` constant; `.expanded { transform: rotate(-90deg); transition: transform .15s }`. Adopters MUST NOT use the `▾ ◀` swap pattern even though it appears simpler — the metric mismatch is observable. Composition: the `[hidden]` CSS pitfall (`dashboard-render-patterns.md §3` — `display: flex` overriding the UA default `[hidden] { display: none }`) is orthogonal and still applies; the rotation pattern is the *indicator* discipline, the `[hidden]` fix is the *content visibility* discipline.

**Pattern 2 — Date-line divider: client-tz day-boundary insertion + sticky positioning**

The chronological message stream MUST insert a date-line divider at every client-local day boundary, with the day computed from `row.timestamp` (epoch ms, client-side `new Date(epoch)`) — NEVER from the wire-format ISO string (the wire string carries sender's tz; the divider must reflect the *viewer's* local-day boundary, not the sender's). The divider element uses `position: sticky; top: 0` so the most-recent day label remains visible during scroll; the sticky-top offset MUST account for the chat-panel header height (not the page header height — a date-line floating behind the chat panel header is a UX bug). Visual canonical: centered day label (locale-dependent — `오늘 / 어제 / YYYY-MM-DD` for Korean, `Today / Yesterday / YYYY-MM-DD` for English) with `~ ~` decorators on either side (rendered via `::before` / `::after` CSS pseudo-elements, not literal characters in the DOM — keeps the divider's text content programmatically accessible as just the date). The scroll container (the message stream itself) MUST have `padding-top: 0` so the sticky divider docks tight to the top edge of its viewport. Composition: this pattern composes with §13.11.3 rule 3 (timestamp obligation + client-local render) — the server stamps `msg.timestamp = Date.now()` if absent (rule 3), and the dashboard uses that epoch for the divider's day computation (this pattern).

**Pattern 3 — A2A attachment chip: mime detection + preview + graceful localPath**

A2A messages carrying attachments (the `value.attachments[]` / `value.zip` / `value.attachment` field-name choice is portable per `dashboard-render-patterns.md §6`) MUST render the attachment metadata as an inline chip inside the message card body — NOT as a separate row beneath the message. The chip composes: mime-icon glyph (emoji or icon font; `📄 / 🖼️ / 🗜️ / 🎵` for text/image/archive/audio) + filename + size + (preview trigger | download trigger). Preview triggers MUST handle both wire shapes: (a) `dataUrl` or `url` field present → inline modal renders the resource; (b) only `localPath` present (the attachment lives on the sender's filesystem, not transported in the envelope) → chip still renders gracefully with the localPath as informational metadata + a "local file, not transported" indicator, NEVER an error or a broken-link icon. Download triggers MUST handle the same two cases (transport vs metadata-only). Rationale for "metadata-only graceful display": targetless / metadata-only attachments are a common emit pattern when the sender means "here's a file I have, name and check it" rather than "here's a file I'm transmitting"; treating the metadata-only case as a broken transport pollutes the dashboard with false-error indicators. Composition: §13.13 application-tier ack — an `AckProcessed` on an attachment message means the recipient agent has *surfaced* the metadata, NOT that the recipient has downloaded the localPath resource (which they cannot do without filesystem access to the sender).

**Pattern 4 — Closed-session connection indicator: present-set based color dot**

Each agent row in the roster (sidebar / dropdown / agent list) MUST render a connection indicator dot whose color reflects the agent's *present membership* in the live `AgentList` from the server — NOT the row's display-visibility state. Canonical color binding: present in `AgentList` → green dot `●`; absent (history-only — the row exists because the agent has sent messages but is not currently connected) → gray dot `●`. The dot updates on every `AgentList` push from the server (§13.9 onboarding handshake group). Tooltip on the dot MUST surface the precise connection state (`connected since <local-tz timestamp>` / `last seen <local-tz timestamp>`) — local-tz, NOT wire-format (composes with Pattern 2's client-local rendering discipline). Composition with §13.13: a `delivered` ack (transport-tier) on a message to a gray-dot agent is wire suspect (the agent is not currently connected to receive); the dashboard MAY surface this with an inline warning ("delivered to inbox, recipient currently offline") rather than escalating silently to commitment-tier wait — closes the "wait forever on a disconnected agent" gap.

**Pattern 5 — Upstream tab re-exposure: present-set sweep, not just delta**

When the roster includes manually-hidden tabs (e.g., the operator collapsed an upstream agent's view because the conversation was finished), the auto-re-expose logic MUST trigger on **every `AgentList` push where the agent is present**, not only on the `absent → present` delta. Rationale: an upstream agent that stays continuously connected (long-lived peer) never produces an `absent → present` delta after initial join; if the operator collapses the tab mid-conversation, the tab stays collapsed forever even though the agent is actively producing messages. The corrected discipline: on every `AgentList`, for each `present` agent, if the agent's tab is currently `hidden`, un-hide it (the next message will re-attract the operator's attention without the operator having to manually re-expose the tab). The `present` sweep MUST be idempotent — re-exposing an already-visible tab is a no-op, not an error. Composition: this is the "long-lived upstream peer" failure mode that the §13.16.9 handshake-group classification (v2.5.2) does not catch — `AgentList` is in the handshake group, so the watcher correctly does NOT wake on each push, but the dashboard MUST still re-evaluate tab visibility on each push regardless of watcher-wake intent.

**Pattern 6 — Upstream A2A classification (receiver-side): source-set-agnostic detection + text relay fallback**

(v2.4.52: everything this pattern says about long-lived `upstream` peers applies equally to `peer`-role peer-mains — both are external emitters whose `source` value may be nonstandard.)

The dashboard's receiver-side A2A-intent detection MUST use the negation form of §13.11.3 rule 2: `source !== "user" && source !== "board" && targetAgentId && targetAgentId !== self`. CRITICALLY, the detection MUST NOT use the positive-set form `source === "agent"` because upstream peer agents emit `source = <their-agentId>` (a nonstandard but conformant source value); the positive-set check silently false-negatives ALL upstream A2A traffic, producing the operator complaint "upstream A2A is invisible on dashboard". The negation form is portable across the standard `source: "agent"` and the upstream variant `source: <agentId>` and any future emitter variant. **Text relay fallback** (the second half of this pattern): the server's outbound routing (§13.16.9 routing decision tree) MUST relay target-unspecified TEXT_MESSAGE envelopes to `wsPrimary` (the main A2A path) when the target-unspecified TEXT_MESSAGE is A2A-intent — i.e., the routing decision tree's fail-safe-default-A2A-intent branch (the fourth branch of the tree) MUST cover TEXT_MESSAGE name too, not just CUSTOM. Without this, upstream agents that emit raw text (without wrapping in CUSTOM) silently drop on the server-side normalization step. Composition: §13.11.3 rule 1 (channel `type` normalization — server stamps `type: "CUSTOM"` when absent) handles the producer-side defect; this pattern handles the *router*-side defect (which is independent of the type stamp).

**Pattern 7 — Board render TEXT_MESSAGE fallback to A2A card (defense layer for non-conformant adopters)**

The receiver-side dashboard MAY detect `TEXT_MESSAGE` envelopes whose `text` field carries a serialized A2A Report (typically as a `[A2A Report]` lead line followed by a fenced JSON code block, e.g., ```` ```json ```` containing `{ type: "Report", ... }`) and **promote** the message into an A2A card render (the `a2acard` surface that §13.16.12 Pattern 6 + Pattern 4 already define for native A2A-intent envelopes). The promotion extracts the JSON payload from the code-block, parses it, and renders the resulting object as if it had arrived as a native `CUSTOM` envelope: name/agentId/msgId/threadId in the envelope summary card; the parsed body as the collapsible JSON body; attachment chips (§13.11 rule 5 / Pattern 3) if `attachments[]` is parseable from the JSON.

**This is a defense-layer pattern, NOT a substitute for the producer-side fix.** The canonical solution is the sender's gateway-client emitting **structured envelopes per §13.11 + §13.11.3 rules 1-5** (named `CUSTOM` with `value` + optional `attachments[]`, not a TEXT_MESSAGE with the same content serialized into `text`). When the sender is a non-conformant adopter — typically a partial reimplementation of the §13.9 / §13.11 contract that has not yet wired its outbound emit path to produce structured envelopes — the receiver's board would otherwise display the serialized JSON as a raw text bubble, losing the A2A-intent surface (no card, no attachment chips, no §13.11 rule 5 mime / dataUrl handling, no §13.13 ack-tier indicators on the rendered surface). Pattern 7 gives the receiver a way to **recover the A2A-intent surface from the serialized text** while the producer-side fix is in flight, preventing the missing-card defect from reaching the operator.

**Implementation discipline**:

1. The detection MUST be a `TEXT_MESSAGE` branch (not a `CUSTOM` branch — the canonical `CUSTOM`-via-§13.11 path is unchanged). The branch runs *after* the normal TEXT_MESSAGE render is computed but *before* it commits to the DOM; if the extraction succeeds, the rendered surface swaps to the A2A card form. If the extraction fails (no `[A2A Report]` lead, no fenced JSON, JSON parse error), the message renders as a normal TEXT_MESSAGE (the fallback gracefully degrades; never errors loudly).
2. The promoted card MUST be visually marked as **fallback-promoted** (e.g., a small `fallback` badge on the card header, or a tooltip "promoted from TEXT_MESSAGE") so the operator can distinguish a canonical `CUSTOM`-rendered card from a Pattern-7-promoted card. The marking serves two purposes: it surfaces *which adopters are still non-conformant* (the operator sees the badge on every Pattern-7 hit), and it preserves audit-trail integrity (the original wire frame was TEXT_MESSAGE, not CUSTOM — the render-tier promotion does not rewrite history).
3. The promotion MUST NOT alter the outbound ack path. Transport-tier `Ack` continues to be the server's mechanic on the original TEXT_MESSAGE frame; commitment-tier `AckProcessed` (if emitted) follows §13.13 normally; the promotion is *render-layer only*.
4. The promotion MUST extract `attachments[]` from the JSON when present, but the chips render against the §13.11 rule 5 graceful-localPath discipline (Pattern 3) — a Pattern-7-promoted card with `source: "embedded"` attachments handles the dataUrl correctly (bytes were in the TEXT_MESSAGE.text serialization); a Pattern-7-promoted card with `source: "local_path"` attachments still renders the chip with the "local file, not transported" indicator (no error). This composes Pattern 7 with Pattern 3 at the chip layer: Pattern 7 supplies the parsed attachment array; Pattern 3 supplies the per-chip render discipline.

**Composition with §13.11 + §13.13 + Pattern 6**: §13.11.3 rule 1 (server stamps `type: "CUSTOM"` when absent) handles the producer-side defect where the sender forgot the `type` field; Pattern 7 handles the producer-side defect where the sender wrapped the whole envelope into TEXT_MESSAGE (a stronger non-conformance — the sender chose the wrong envelope shape, not just omitted a field). Pattern 6 (source-set-agnostic detection + text relay fallback) handles the *router*-side defect where the server failed to relay a target-unspecified TEXT_MESSAGE; Pattern 7 runs *after* the routing layer has already delivered the TEXT_MESSAGE to the recipient — it is the *render*-side complement that catches the case Pattern 6 cannot (a TEXT_MESSAGE that was correctly routed but is in the wrong shape).

**Composition with the §13.16.10 pre-send probe**: Pattern 7 promotion does NOT alter the cursor advancement discipline. A Pattern-7-promoted card counts as a normal meaningful inbound for cursor purposes (the seen-msgId LRU per §13.13.2 v0.4 indexes by the TEXT_MESSAGE's outer `id`, not by the synthesized inner `msgId` if any). The pre-send probe's meaningful-inbound filter (the §13.16.9 v2.5.2 A2A-intent allowlist applied on the `name` field) should be augmented to include `TEXT_MESSAGE-A2A-promoted` for adopters running Pattern 7 — i.e., when the watcher / pre-send probe finds a TEXT_MESSAGE whose text body matches the Pattern 7 detection regex, the probe SHOULD treat it as meaningful (same as a native A2A-intent name) until the producer-side fix lands.

**Lifecycle expectation**: Pattern 7 is a **transitional defense layer**. Adopters should view Pattern 7 hits as a backlog signal (each Pattern-7-promoted card is an instance of a non-conformant producer that needs fixing); the discipline target is *zero Pattern 7 hits* over a steady operating window. When all adopters in a deployment emit structured envelopes per §13.11, Pattern 7 becomes dormant but is not removed — keeping it in place protects against regression (a future implementation reverting to TEXT_MESSAGE wrapping would not silently lose the A2A-intent surface).

**Composition with `dashboard-render-patterns.md`**: the reference doc carries the concrete render-tier patterns (function names, CSS selectors, file paths in the vanilla-DOM master copy under `constellation/reference/dashboard/`); this §13.16.12 carries the protocol-tier discipline that the reference doc instantiates. An adopter MAY ship a non-vanilla dashboard implementation as long as the §13.16.12 invariants hold; the reference doc is the *suggested* implementation, not the *contract*. The reference doc's eight sections (introduction · A2A row interaction · collapse `[hidden]` CSS pitfall · board render card form · date-line · attachment chip · connection indicator · upstream A2A general-tab detection) correspond to this sub-section's seven patterns (Pattern 7 added in v2.5.13 — the dashboard-render-patterns reference doc may grow a §9 "TEXT_MESSAGE-to-A2A-card fallback" section in a future revision to mirror the protocol-tier addition here) plus two prior-cycle patterns (§2 row interaction + §4 board render card form, already absorbed at the protocol tier through §13.16.9 + §13.11.3 in v2.5.1).

**Scope**: tier-1 protocol body augmentation only. The wire format is unchanged (Patterns 1-5 + Pattern 7 are render-tier behavior; Pattern 6 codifies a receiver-side detection rule + a routing tree branch that v2.5.1 §13.16.9 already documented). The reference doc `dashboard-render-patterns.md` is unchanged in v2.5.13 — its eight sections continue to be the renderer's concrete manual, while this §13.16.12 is the new tier-1 SSoT entry. Downstream Constellation adopters who built against v2.5.1 §13.16.9 already cover Pattern 6's protocol-tier surface; Patterns 1-5 + Pattern 7 are render-only and codified-as-tier-1 by this sub-section. The dashboard reference master copy under `constellation/reference/dashboard/` (the vanilla-DOM implementation) ships the §13.16.12 patterns by example (Pattern 7 implementation lands upstream as `wsExtractA2aReport` helper + TEXT_MESSAGE branch in app.js); adopters re-skinning the dashboard MUST preserve the §13.16.12 invariants while they replace the render layer.

### 13.16.13 Ultrasafe A2A-intent family — pre-release simulated-pentest wire-spec (v2.4.3)

**Purpose**: this sub-section is the wire-level SSoT for the five Ultrasafe A2A-intent names added to §13.16.9 in v2.4.3 (`ULTRASAFE_FINDING` / `ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY` / `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` / `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE` / `MPCVD_COORDINATION`). It companion-pairs to `Ultrasafe.md §18` (Constellation integration — 5 신규 intent runtime wire) the way `Hyperbrief.md §8` companions §13.16.9's Hyperbrief lines: this section owns the *Constellation-side* contract (envelope shape, ack-tier mapping, board-mirror policy, dual-mode behavior); the Ultrasafe spec owns the *runtime-side* contract (when each intent emits, who consumes it, how findings flow through the 8-agent fan-out + 3-iteration AND-gate). The two sections MUST stay in lockstep — when one updates a field or an ack-tier, the other updates the same cycle.

**Why a dedicated sub-section** (not just the §13.16.9 line): the Ultrasafe family carries a **dual-mode discipline** (advisory v0.2.x → blocking v0.3+) that the Hyperbrief family does not — every envelope carries an `advisory_mode: boolean` flag (or `mode: 'advisory' | 'blocking'`), and the ack-tier expected by the recipient depends on the mode. Encoding the mode-mapping inline in §13.16.9 would bloat the allowlist beyond readability; the dedicated sub-section gives the dual-mode contract its own surface and lets §13.16.9 stay enumeration-shaped.

**Envelope shapes per intent** (canonical CUSTOM wire form per §13.11):

1. **`ULTRASAFE_FINDING`** — per-attacker finding emit (one envelope per finding; an attacker emits 0..N findings per iteration).
   - `value.finding_id` — stable UUID per finding (LRU-deduplicable across iterations).
   - `value.attacker_role` — one of `ai-llm-redteam` · `web-api-attacker` · `supply-chain-auditor` · `crypto-reviewer` · `social-engineer` · `methodology-compliance` · `threat-model-lifecycle` · `synthesizer`. Synthesizer findings carry `category: 'cross-axis-correlation'` and reference 2+ source `finding_id`s.
   - `value.severity` — closed enum `info` · `low` · `medium` · `high` · `critical`. Severity mapping to ack-tier: see "ack-tier per intent" table below.
   - `value.category` — free-form short string (e.g., `prompt-injection`, `sqli`, `dep-vuln`, `key-mgmt`); the synthesizer uses this for cross-axis dedup.
   - `value.evidence` — array of evidence atoms (`{ type: 'file-ref' | 'wire-capture' | 'test-output' | 'doc-quote', ref, snippet }`); the file-ref / doc-quote variants MUST honor §13.14 redaction (no env-specific identifiers in public-board mirror).
   - `value.reproduction` — short reproduction recipe (commands, inputs, expected vs actual); blocking-mode v0.3+ requires non-empty `reproduction`.
   - `value.confidence` — `low` · `medium` · `high` (attacker self-rated; the synthesizer downgrades on cross-axis dispute).
   - `value.iteration` — integer 1..N (which iteration of the ≥3-iteration loop produced this finding).
   - `value.advisory_mode` — boolean; `true` in v0.2.x, `false` in v0.3+ blocking. The recipient's ack-tier expectation switches on this field.

2. **`ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY`** — boundary marker between iterations of the ≥3-iteration loop (one envelope per boundary; for an N-iteration run, N+1 boundaries exist — pre-iter-1 + post-iter-1 + … + post-iter-N).
   - `value.boundary_id` — stable UUID per boundary.
   - `value.iteration_count` — integer (the iteration *just completed*; 0 for the pre-iter-1 boundary).
   - `value.clean_signal_state` — object `{ monotonic_finding_reduction: boolean, regression_free: boolean, coverage_floor_met: boolean, two_iter_consecutive: boolean, composite_AND_pass: boolean }` — the 4-condition AND-gate from `Ultrasafe.md §15`. `composite_AND_pass` is `true` only when all four sub-conditions are `true`; the loop terminates on the first boundary where `composite_AND_pass === true` AND `iteration_count >= 3`.
   - `value.finding_count_delta` — `{ total: integer, by_severity: { info, low, medium, high, critical }, by_attacker_role: { … } }` (signed integer delta vs previous boundary; negative = improvement, positive = regression).
   - `value.coverage_summary` — `{ axes_covered: integer, axes_total: integer, gaps: string[] }` (the 17-axis coverage summary; `gaps` lists axes that produced no findings AND no clean signal).

3. **`ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE`** — publish-time gate state (one envelope per publish attempt; emitted by the PreToolUse hook `ultrasafe-trigger.cjs` immediately before the publish-equivalent command).
   - `value.gate_id` — stable UUID per gate evaluation.
   - `value.publish_target` — short descriptor of the publish surface (`npm:<pkg>` · `pypi:<pkg>` · `git-push:<repo>@<tag>` · `docker:<image>:<tag>` — the `Ultrasafe.md` §17 PreToolUse trigger surface enumeration).
   - `value.gate_decision` — closed enum `advisory_report_only` (v0.2.x — report-only, publish proceeds) · `blocking_user_gate` (v0.3+ — requires user gate via paired `DECISION_REQUEST`) · `clean_signal_clear` (≥3 iterations completed with `composite_AND_pass`, no gate intervention needed).
   - `value.mode` — `advisory` (v0.2.x) or `blocking` (v0.3+); the `advisory_mode` boolean on `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` mirrors this at the envelope tier.
   - `value.reason` — short prose explaining the decision (`"≥3 iterations completed, composite_AND_pass=true on iter 4"` · `"high-severity finding F-7f3a in iter 2, advisory report emitted, publish proceeds (v0.2 advisory mode)"` · `"critical finding F-9c2b in iter 1, blocking gate requires user decision"`).
   - `value.finding_summary` — `{ total: integer, by_severity: { … }, top_findings: [ { finding_id, severity, category, attacker_role } ] }` (top findings ranked by severity then confidence; top-K with K=5 default).
   - `value.iteration_count` — final iteration count at gate evaluation.
   - `value.paired_decision_id` — populated when `gate_decision === 'blocking_user_gate'`; carries the `decision_id` of the paired Hyperbrief `DECISION_REQUEST` so the board renders them as one card (same `parentId` linkage pattern as `DECISION_REQUEST` ↔ `HyperbriefCard`).

4. **`SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE`** — external disclosure entry (one envelope per disclosure intake event; emitted by the disclosure-handling adapter when an external report arrives via email / GitHub Security Advisory / bug-bounty platform / direct A2A).
   - `value.disclosure_id` — stable UUID per disclosure.
   - `value.reporter_handle` — reporter's identifier (GitHub handle, email-derived stable ID, bug-bounty username); MUST be redacted to a stable opaque ID on the board mirror (§13.14 — public-board mirror must not leak external identities pre-coordination).
   - `value.disclosure_summary` — short prose of the disclosed vulnerability (recipient-side summary, not the full reporter narrative — the full narrative lives in the disclosure ledger with restricted access).
   - `value.severity_estimate` — recipient's initial severity estimate (closed enum same as `ULTRASAFE_FINDING.value.severity`); refined on triage.
   - `value.received_at` — ISO timestamp.
   - `value.intake_channel` — closed enum `email` · `github_security_advisory` · `bug_bounty` · `direct_a2a` · `other`.
   - `value.triage_owner_agentId` — optional; the agentId assigned to triage (may be empty on intake, populated on first triage hop).

5. **`MPCVD_COORDINATION`** — Multi-Party Coordinated Vulnerability Disclosure envelope (emitted when a disclosure escalates to multi-party coordination — multiple vendors / multiple downstream consumers / CERT/CC-style coordination).
   - `value.coordination_id` — stable UUID per coordination event.
   - `value.parties` — array of `{ party_id, party_name, role: 'reporter' | 'maintainer' | 'downstream' | 'coordinator' | 'cert', contact_handle, status: 'pending' | 'acknowledged' | 'embargoed' | 'disclosed' | 'withdrawn' }`. The `contact_handle` is redacted on board mirror (§13.14).
   - `value.timeline` — `{ disclosure_received: iso, embargo_start: iso, embargo_end: iso (== embargo_until), coordinated_disclosure: iso, public_advisory: iso }` (any phase may be `null` until reached).
   - `value.embargo_until` — ISO timestamp (canonical convenience field equal to `timeline.embargo_end`); MUST be honored by all parties' downstream emit paths (no `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` / `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` cross-reference to the coordinated vulnerability before `embargo_until`).
   - `value.severity_consensus` — `{ severity: enum, cvss_vector: string, agreed_by: party_id[] }` (severity consensus across parties; `agreed_by` MUST include majority of parties for the consensus to bind).
   - `value.disclosure_linkage` — `{ source_disclosure_id: uuid }` (the originating `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE.value.disclosure_id` that escalated to MPCVD).

**Ack-tier per intent (v2.4.3 mapping — composes with §13.13 3-tier + Hyperbrief `decided` 4th tier)**:

| intent | v0.2.x (advisory) ack_tier | v0.3+ (blocking) ack_tier | rationale |
|--------|---------------------------|---------------------------|-----------|
| `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` | `received` (server hop) | `acknowledged` (recipient surfaced) — `decided` for severity ≥ high (paired Hyperbrief `DECISION_REQUEST`) | advisory: report-only, no recipient action required; blocking: high-severity findings trigger paired decision gate |
| `ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY` | `received` | `received` | boundary markers are informational across both modes; the 4-condition AND-gate evaluation is a client-side computation, not a recipient-action surface |
| `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` | `received` (advisory report-only) | `decided` (blocking — user MUST clear the gate; reuses Hyperbrief `decided` tier) | advisory mode: publish proceeds regardless of recipient state; blocking mode: publish blocks on `decided` ack from paired `DECISION_REQUEST` |
| `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE` | `acknowledged` | `acknowledged` | intake confirmation surfaces to the reporter side that the disclosure was received; mode-independent |
| `MPCVD_COORDINATION` | `decided` | `decided` | consensus formation requires party-side `decided` ack to bind; mode-independent (coordination is by definition multi-party-blocking even when individual finding flow is advisory) |

The `decided` tier reuses the Hyperbrief application-tier extension (§13.16.9 `ack_tier='decided'`) — the same 4-tier ladder `received → acknowledged → decided` applies. Adopters who built the Hyperbrief `decided` handler against the §13.13 ladder get the Ultrasafe `decided` handler for free (same code path; the intent name discriminates the downstream consumer).

**Board-mirror policy**:

- **`ULTRASAFE_FINDING`** — board mirror renders as an A2A card with severity-colored badge (info=gray · low=blue · medium=yellow · high=orange · critical=red); collapsible body shows the finding fields. Evidence atoms render per type (file-ref → file-path chip; wire-capture → code block; doc-quote → blockquote — all redacted per §13.14). When `value.advisory_mode === true`, the card carries an `advisory` ribbon on the header to distinguish from blocking-mode findings.
- **`ULTRASAFE_ITERATION_BOUNDARY`** — board mirror renders as a timeline divider (similar shape to §13.16.12 Pattern 2 date-line, but for iteration boundaries within an Ultrasafe run). The divider shows `iteration N → N+1` with the 4-condition AND-gate state as a small badge row (4 dots, green for pass / red for fail). The terminal boundary (where `composite_AND_pass === true` AND `iteration_count >= 3`) renders with a `clean-signal-clear` end-marker.
- **`ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE`** — board mirror renders as a gate card with publish-target prominently displayed; `gate_decision` colors the card (advisory_report_only=gray · blocking_user_gate=red · clean_signal_clear=green). When `gate_decision === 'blocking_user_gate'`, the card pairs with the linked `DECISION_REQUEST` card (same `parentId` linkage; renders as one composite card with the gate state + decision UI side by side).
- **`SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE`** — board mirror renders with reporter identifiers redacted (the public-board MUST NOT expose external reporter handles pre-coordination); the redacted card shows `intake_channel`, `severity_estimate`, `received_at`, `disclosure_summary` (recipient-side summary, never reporter narrative). Triage-owner agentId is shown if populated.
- **`MPCVD_COORDINATION`** — board mirror renders as a coordination card with parties as a chip row (one chip per party, each chip showing role + status with the party's `contact_handle` redacted). Timeline renders as a Gantt-style horizontal strip with the current phase highlighted. Embargo-until is prominent and the card carries a `pre-embargo` ribbon when `now < embargo_until` (signaling that no downstream finding cross-references are permitted yet).

**Composition with §13.16.10 pre-send probe**: all five Ultrasafe intents are in the A2A-intent allowlist (§13.16.9), so the §13.16.10 pre-send probe filter catches them as meaningful inbound. An agent in the middle of an Ultrasafe iteration MUST surface any inbound `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` (from sibling attackers in the same fan-out) before its own next emit — the synthesizer's cross-axis dedup depends on having all sibling findings in working context before it correlates. An agent in the middle of a release gate evaluation MUST surface any inbound `SECURITY_DISCLOSURE_INTAKE` or `MPCVD_COORDINATION` envelope before emitting `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` — a fresh disclosure may bind a new embargo that the gate evaluation MUST honor.

**Composition with §13.16.12 Pattern 7 fallback**: non-conformant adopters that wrap an Ultrasafe envelope in `TEXT_MESSAGE` (rather than canonical `CUSTOM`) MUST use the Pattern 7 prefix `[Ultrasafe <intent_short> | id=<id> | severity=<severity> | mode=<advisory|blocking>]` so the receiver-side Pattern 7 promotion correctly extracts the JSON body and renders as an A2A card. The `<intent_short>` token mapping: `finding` · `iter-boundary` · `release-gate` · `disclosure-intake` · `mpcvd`. The receiver's `wsExtractA2aReport` helper (the v2.5.13 upstream reference implementation) gains a parallel `wsExtractUltrasafeReport` branch for these prefixes; both helpers run on the same TEXT_MESSAGE path with disjoint detection regexes.

**Cross-module wire connections** (the v2.4.3 cut runs three integrations):

- **Ultrasafe ↔ Hyperbrief** — `ULTRASAFE_FINDING` with `severity ≥ high` (advisory mode) or `severity ≥ medium` (blocking mode) triggers a paired `DECISION_REQUEST` emission. The pair shares a `parentId` linkage; the board renders them as a composite card (finding details + decision gate side by side). `ULTRASAFE_RELEASE_GATE` in blocking mode (`gate_decision === 'blocking_user_gate'`) REQUIRES a paired `DECISION_REQUEST` co-emission — the `value.paired_decision_id` field carries the linkage. The Hyperbrief skill (`hyperbrief-trigger-check`) gains an `ultrasafe` source class in its trigger rubric per `Hyperbrief.md §2`; the skill's IR carries `source_class: 'ultrasafe-release-gate'` on these paired emissions.
- **Ultrasafe ↔ Greatpractice** — ratified findings (findings that persist across ≥2 iterations in the same run, or recur across ≥2 separate runs) flow into Greatpractice's 5-axis maturation gate as macro/mezzo entry candidates. The `Ultrasafe.md §16` MCP tool `ultrasafe_finding_aggregate` exposes a `--export-greatpractice-candidates` flag that emits the candidate set as a JSON file consumable by Greatpractice's `entry-frontmatter.schema.json`.
