The EG repo (`SoliEstre/EstreGenesis`) is named explicitly because it is public-shipped.

#### 13.22.2 Two-level abstraction — Level 1 (virtual PR, A2A-only) vs Level 2 (Github PR, provider-mediated)

The same wire vocabulary (§13.22.3) and state machine (§13.22.8) describe two physical realizations of a "PR." Which applies is a function of *who operates the source and target sides* and *what file-system access the receiving side holds*. `PRRequest.level` is an explicit `1 | 2` payload field; it defaults to `2` when absent.

- **Level 1 — virtual PR (A2A-only path)**. No provider-side PR object is created. Applicable when source and target sides **share an operator** AND **both hold direct repo-level file-system access**. The receiving side (holding commit-push authority on the target repo) reads the `sourceContentRef` carried by `PRRequest`, applies the change directly to its local checkout of the target repo, commits, and pushes — using A2A envelopes only for review / ack signaling. `gh pr create` is skipped; MERGED ≡ "commit pushed to the target's integration branch."
- **Level 2 — Github PR (provider-mediated path)**. The receiving side invokes `gh pr create` against the target provider; the PR exists as a real provider object; review and merge flow through the provider UI / API, with A2A envelopes mirroring state. Applicable when source and target are operated by different parties, OR the PR is cross-org, OR the target's integration policy requires a provider-side PR object (required-status-checks, provider-tier audit trail).

**Selection rule**. When `category == trusted-mirror` AND operator-shares-target AND target-repo-direct-access both hold, **Level 1 is the default**; otherwise Level 2. The receiving side MUST validate the requested `level` against its capability matrix (direct push to `targetRepo`? operator-shared?) and MUST reject a mismatch with a capability-mismatch reason; the sender MAY retry with the other level. The §13.22.8 state machine is `level`-discriminated: both levels traverse the same five logical states, but the transition triggers and the MERGED realization differ.

#### 13.22.3 Wire vocabulary — five new CUSTOM types

Five new `CUSTOM` types, all layered above §13.13 (server-stamped `msgId`, server-auto `Ack{delivered}`, recipient `AckProcessed`). All are application-tier emissions — none server-auto-emitted. All apply to both levels; per-type level-discriminated fields flagged inline.

| Name | Direction | Required fields | Optional fields | Server filter / authority gate |
|------|-----------|-----------------|-----------------|--------------------------------|
| `PRRequest` | any agent → PR-bot / repo-owner agent | `sourceRepo`, `sourceContentRef`, `targetRepo`, `targetBranch`, `title`, `body`, `level: 1\|2` (default `2`) | `labels[]`, `reviewers[]`, `category`, `slaEta` | Validates repos in the known-repo registry; for `level==1`, validates the receiver's capability matrix |
| `PRDraftReady` | PR-bot (L2) / receiving-side (L1) → requester | `for: msgId`, `draftRef`, `checksPending[]` | `prUrl` (L2), `headBranch`, `dryRun` | Validates `for` references a real `PRRequest` from a registered requester |
| `PRReviewAck` | reviewer-role agent → requester | `for: draftRef`, `verdict: approve\|request-changes\|comment`, `reviewBody` | `inlineComments[]`, `slaEta`, `reviewedAt` | Validates emitter role against the per-repo reviewer policy |
| `PRMergeRequest` / `PRMergeAck` | merge-authority → PR-bot / receiving-side; back to requester | `for: draftRef`, `mergeStrategy` (L2) | `commitTitle`, `deleteSourceBranch`, `dryRun` | `PRMergeRequest`: **strict** — only `role==main` for the target repo; non-main rejected + logged to `decisions` |
| `PRStatusUpdate` | PR-bot (L2) / receiving-side (L1) → watchers | `draftRef`, `level`, `state: draft\|open\|changes_requested\|approved\|merged\|closed` | `checks` (L2), `reviewState`, `nextSlaCheckAt` | Validates emitter against bot-identity registry (L2) / capability matrix (L1) |

**`sourceContentRef.kind` enum** (closed — receivers MUST reject unknown values): `branch-ref` (`git fetch` + `checkout FETCH_HEAD -- .`), `inline-files-diff` (`git apply <filesDiff>`), `inline-section-mirror` (apply `body` to `targetPath` per `mergeStrategy`, then `git add <targetPath>` ONLY, commit — NO branch-fetch). **Fail-safe** (load-bearing): unrecognized `kind` → reject with `PRRequestRejected { reason: 'unknown-source-content-kind', kind }`, MUST NOT fall through to a default (an unknown kind falling through to `branch-ref` triggers `checkout FETCH_HEAD -- .` = wholesale target-repo overwrite — the dogfood near-disaster).

#### 13.22.4 Agent topology — local-bridge command (adopted)

Three realizations of the PR-bot role: **(a) Dedicated A2A agent** (long-running `pr-bot` holding provider credentials; clean isolation but needs a credential store + deploy surface); **(b) Local-bridge command — ADOPTED** (extend `local-bridge` with a `createPR` port running in the operator's IDE alongside their `gh`/`git` auth — no separate credentials; the flow: agent emits `PRRequest` → local-bridge invokes provider CLI [L2] or applies-commits-pushes locally [L1] → emits `PRDraftReady`); **(c) Hybrid** (dedicated bot for cross-machine/separate-identity, local-bridge for same-operator; deferred). Topology (b) is adopted because it reuses the operator's existing CLI auth — no credential store in scope. It is also the natural home for **Level 1**: the bridge already holds direct file-system access on both sides when they share an operator. Topology (a)/(c) are phase-2/3 expansions (a credential-management RRP gates (a)).

#### 13.22.5 Approval discipline — trusted-mirror / standard (per-PR opt-in default) / emergency

The autonomous-execution external-publish gate is canonical: a PR to a repo other than the one the agent operates in is an external publish requiring user opt-in *unless* a pre-authorized policy specifies otherwise.

- **`trusted-mirror`** (pre-authorized) — a spec-mirror PR where the diff is *already reviewed in the source repo* and the target is *the deterministic mirror surface*. The pre-authorization lives in `state.json.pr_system.trusted_mirrors[]` as `(sourceRepo, sourceContentRef) → (targetRepo, targetContentRef)` pairings. A matching `PRRequest { category: 'trusted-mirror' }` is created without per-PR prompt; per-deployment policy MAY rate-limit (≤1 per pair per 24h) to catch runaway automation.
- **`standard`** (per-PR user opt-in — **the default**) — any PR not matching a trusted-mirror entry. The receiving side surfaces the request via the live board `decisions` panel (§13.17 — the canonical structured-choice surface); the user explicitly approves; on approval the PR is created. This is the external-publish gate's default.
- **`emergency`** (out-of-band approval reference) — for hotfix mirrors faster than the user can respond; carries `outOfBandApprovalRef` (a `decisions` msgId the user pre-approved), validated against the board's persistence. Carries a TOCTOU risk surface; **deferred to phase 3**. Phase 1/1b ship `trusted-mirror` + `standard` only.

**`inline-section-mirror` invariants** (the canonical spec-mirror content form): (1) **`git add` isolation** — after applying `body`, `git add <targetPath>` ONLY, never `-A`/`.` (a fallthrough commits every untracked file — the dogfood defect); (2) **No branch-fetch**; (3) **Existence check** — verify `targetPath` exists before append, else reject `inline-mirror-target-missing`; (4) **Dry-run `abs+exists` log** — when gated OFF, log `abs=<resolved> exists=<bool>` so path defects surface pre-live. **`targetPath` base** = relative to the receiver's repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`), deterministic + portable; process-cwd / absolute / sub-tree bases are NOT used.

#### 13.22.6 Cross-repo content sourcing — β′ mirror-branch-on-target (adopted) + α small-diff fallback

- **β′ — mirror branch on the TARGET repo (Level 2 primary, adopted)**. Instead of pushing a branch to the source repo and fetching cross-repo, the local-bridge pushes source content to a `mirror/<topic>` branch on the **target** repo, then opens the PR from that target-side mirror branch into the target's integration branch — effectively intra-repo at the provider level, no cross-repo provider authorization. (Trade-off: requires push access to the target repo; the mirror branch is transient, relying on provider auto-delete-head-branch.)
- **α — inline diff (small-diff fallback)**. Unified-diff bytes in `PRRequest.filesDiff`, applied by the receiver. Used only for small Level-2 diffs (< ~50 KB); breaks at scale (~80 KB+ outbox split-delivery).
- **β (source-repo branch) / γ (fork) NOT used** in scope — β′ supersedes β (sidesteps cross-repo provider read-auth). **Level 1** sourcing is implicit (receiver reads `sourceContentRef` directly; no mirror branch). **`trusted_mirrors.targetRepo` alias** — the registry SHOULD use a stable alias (default `"hub"`) not the real repo id; `matchTrustedMirror` resolves: (1) `state.json.pr_system.target_aliases`, (2) `git remote get-url origin` parsed to `org/repo`, (3) reject `unknown-target-repo-alias`. The wire carries only the alias; the real id stays operator-local (§13.14).

#### 13.22.7 Authority + permission — per-repo role mapping

An agent's role is a function of **(agent identity, target repo)**, not identity alone:

| Repo | EG agent role | `<hub-repo>` main agent role |
|------|---------------|------------------------------|
| EG (`SoliEstre/EstreGenesis`) | `main` | `peer/upstream` |
| `<hub-repo>` | `peer/upstream` | `main` |

The merge-authority gate is **strict**: only an agent with `role == main` *for the target repo* may emit `PRMergeRequest` (server `wsPrMergeReject`; non-main rejected + logged to `decisions`). Independent of provider ACL drift — the protocol authority chain is deterministic. Load-bearing consequence: when EG (`main` for EG) issues `PRMergeRequest` against `<hub-repo>` (where EG is `peer/upstream`), the request is **rejected** — merge authority on `<hub-repo>` rests with the `<hub-repo>` main-role agent. Other types follow the §13.22.3 server-filter column.

#### 13.22.8 State machine — 5-state PR lifecycle (level-discriminated)

Both levels traverse the same logical states. **Level 2**: provider events (translated by the bridge into `PRStatusUpdate`) + review-authority emissions drive transitions; MERGED ≡ `gh pr merge` succeeded. **Level 1**: A2A envelope events drive transitions (no provider state); `PRDraftReady` carries the staged commit SHA; `PRMergeRequest` triggers commit-to-integration-branch + push; MERGED ≡ push succeeded (SHA reported in `PRMergeAck`).

```text
   PRRequest received → DRAFT ──(created [L2] / staged [L1])──→ OPEN ──(reviewer engages)──→ IN_REVIEW
                          │                                                                     │
                          └──(rejected: invalid / unauthorized / capability mismatch)──→ CLOSED │
   IN_REVIEW ──(PRReviewAck approve)──→ APPROVED ──(PRMergeRequest [role==main] + PRMergeAck)──→ MERGED
   IN_REVIEW ──(PRReviewAck request-changes)──→ CHANGES_REQUESTED ──(requester follow-up)──→ IN_REVIEW (loop)
   (from any state → CLOSED: superseded or withdrawn)
```

**Composition with §13.19** — a PR past SLA in `IN_REVIEW`/`CHANGES_REQUESTED` is a §13.19.2 quasi-deadlock candidate; the reviewer's `slaEta` on `request-changes` is a §13.19.7 `ReviewSLAAck`-shaped commitment; breach routes the §13.20 nudge ladder (polite → explicit → deadline → human), tier-4 escalates to the `decisions` panel with `class: 'pr-stalled'`. **Composition with §13.13** — every emission gets server-auto `Ack{delivered}`; `AckProcessed` on request-parse + `PRDraftReady` on actual creation preserves the three-grade stratification. **Already-in-target cherry-pick skip (L1 merge handler)** — in Level 1 the receiving bridge already committed the staged change to the target's local integration branch at apply time; on `PRMergeRequest`, check `git merge-base --is-ancestor <draftRef> <targetBranch>` BEFORE cherry-pick: if ancestor, skip cherry-pick → `git push` directly; else cherry-pick then push (avoids duplicate-commit). Level 2 unaffected (`gh pr merge` against a separate provider object).

#### 13.22.9 Cross-links

- **§13.9** — supplies the role model the §13.22.7 strict merge gate extends to per-repo dimensionality.
- **§13.11** — every PR-lifecycle emission is a board safe-point + MUST emit to the board (not bilateral-only); `PRStatusUpdate` is the periodic emission (same heartbeat-ban exception class as §13.19 / §13.20 — fires on lifecycle events).
- **§13.13** — the substrate; every §13.22 emission gets server-auto `Ack{delivered}`; `PRDraftReady`/`PRReviewAck` compose with `AckProcessed`.
- **§13.14** — §13.22 follows redaction in its own text (`<hub-repo>` placeholder + `targetRepo` alias keep the production path off the wire); the §13.14/§13.15 mirror PR is the *first artifact* §13.22 mirrors.
- **§13.16.9** — the five new `CUSTOM` types are subject to the A2A-intent allowlist; the §13.22.3 server-filter column is the per-type authority-gate extension.
- **§13.17** — `category: standard` `PRRequest` surfaces user-approval via the `decisions` panel, NOT inline `AskUserQuestion`; tier-4 PR-stalled escalations route the same way.
- **§13.19** — a PR past SLA in `IN_REVIEW` is a quasi-deadlock candidate; the §13.19.6 ladder applies on breach.
- **§13.20** — a PR-stalled blocker IS a §13.20 blocker; the nudge ladder applies, tier-4 carries `class: 'pr-stalled'`.

#### 13.22.10 Optional server-side PR observe tier (v2.4.16 — board visibility, slightly above pure relay)

The base Constellation server treats `CUSTOM` as **pure relay** — it routes without interpreting payloads (§13.13 layer split). The PR system's five types are the one place a server MAY opt in to *slightly* more, and that excess must be declared, bounded, and opt-in:

- **(a) Observe set** — the server watches the five §13.22.3 types as they relay and projects the PR lifecycle onto the board (per-PR card/panel tracking the §13.22.8 five-state machine). Observation is read-only over messages already in flight; it never alters, delays, or originates PR traffic.
- **(b) Merge-authority gate** — `wsPrMergeReject`: a `PRMergeRequest` from any agent whose role is not `main` *for the target repo* is rejected and logged to the `decisions` panel. This is the server-side half of the §13.22.7 strict authority chain — the one observe-tier behavior that is *more* than observation, justified because merge is the protocol's only irreversible transition.
- **(c) Strictly optional** — the protocol is complete without this tier: Level 1 and Level 2 both function agent-side only. The tier adds visibility (a) and authority hardening (b); absence degrades neither correctness nor the lifecycle.
- **(d) Declared exception, no creep** — when enabled, the server is content-aware for exactly these five types and nothing else. Register the tier as an explicit, named exception to the §13.13 layer split; extending content-awareness to any other `CUSTOM` family requires its own §-level case — the PR tier is not a precedent for general payload inspection.
- **(e) Reference implementation** — adopter-side (hub): a server `_PR_CUSTOM` observe set + `PRStatusUpdate` observation + the `wsPrMergeReject` strict gate, shipped additively alongside the local-bridge `createPR` port (dry-run default, live-PR env opt-in). EG ships this spec tier; the implementation stays adopter-side per the §13.22 provenance note.


**Provenance**: distilled from EG RRP `constellation/reference/docs/archive/2026-06-01-a2a-pr-system-rrp.md` into the adopted Phase 1 (Level 2 provider-mediated) + Phase 1b (Level 1 A2A-only) form, dogfood-validated by the §13.14/§13.15 mirror as the first protocol-mediated PR (three structural defects — `sourceContentRef.kind` placeholder lookup, missing `inline-section-mirror` handler, `targetPath` base ambiguity — surfaced and resolved by the dry-run + review + `abs+exists` gate stack before any external publish). The PR-bot reference implementation lives adopter-side (local-bridge `createPR` port + server-side five-type observer + `wsPrMergeReject` strict gate); EG ships the protocol spec.

### 13.23 Backend registry + board-worker projection (C1)

#### 13.23.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.24 (2026-06-13). Absorbed from the `netwaif/multi-agent-starter` benchmark (MIT — external-framework attribution per the EstreUX rule) as candidate **C1**, adjusted EG-native. The starter's `_shared/backends.json` is an **active call dispatcher** (`call_worker.sh` invokes models). EG is **turn-based** — agents pick their own model at session start; the orchestrator never invokes them. So the same `role → model → connection` data is repurposed: **not a dispatcher but a declarative truth + verification + visualization surface**. Direct motivation: the 2026-06-11 board-observer model swap (Sonnet→Opus) had to be tracked by memory alone — who-is-which-model lived nowhere declarative. This section mechanizes that gap.

#### 13.23.2 The registry (`backends.json`)
- Schema: `{ board, agents: [{ agentId, role, model, connection, board }] }`.
- `role` ∈ {`main`, `board-worker`, `local`, `upstream`, `collab`, `peer` (v2.4.52)} · `connection` ∈ {`bridge`, `local`, …} · `board` ∈ {`self`, `hub`, `self+hub`}.
- **Default location** = the Constellation coordination domain: reference example at `constellation/reference/dashboard/backends.json`; a deployment places its own instance wherever its coordination state lives (this maintenance workspace: `collab-self/backends.json`).
- **Re-sync preserve rule (v2.4.46)** — `backends.json` is *deployment config, not runtime*. Because the reference example sits inside the `dashboard/` copy-set (and the dashboard's default fetch is the relative `./backends.json`), a wholesale vendor-copy re-sync clobbers the deployment's instance (board title, roster). Adapters keep `backends.json` on the re-sync **preserve-list** (or re-apply it after sync) — surfaced by a downstream adapter's Migration-B full re-sync overwriting its branding.
- It is **declarative truth, not a dispatcher** — turn-based agents are never invoked from it; it records what each agent *is*, for verification + projection. Absent file → graceful degradation everywhere (no board-worker split, no badges).

#### 13.23.3 board-worker is a projected role, not a wire role
The server role model (§13.1) derives role from key-kind (collab/upstream) + `WS_PRIMARY_AGENT` (main), else `local`. Adding a `board-worker` *wire* role would require server + key-system changes. Instead board-worker is a **dashboard overlay**: the wire role stays `local`; the dashboard reads `backends.json` and re-classifies any agent declared `role: board-worker` into its own group. Fully decoupled — zero server/protocol change. (The board-worker is the agent that maintains the live board — done/current/planned/decisions — on main's behalf.)

#### 13.23.4 Dashboard projection (board-worker tab group)
- A dedicated **board-worker group** sits between 메인 and 로컬, containing **(a)** the board-worker channel tab and **(b)** a `🔀 Main↔Board` monitor — the main↔board-worker A2A stream, split out of `🔀 Main↔Local` exactly as `🔀 Main↔Collab` is split for collab peers (§13.9 parallel).
- **Role/model badge** — each agent tab carries its declared model (from `backends.json`) as a compact badge.
- **Color** — board-worker inherits the former local hue (green `#39d353`); the generic local role moves to blue (`#4a9ed8`); the `--ws-role-*` SSoT is unified in the same cut. Deliberately **not amber** — amber is reserved for Superscalar §4 Andon speculative lanes. Peer (v2.4.52) takes rose (`#d84a9e`).
- **Peer tab group (v2.4.52)** — a dedicated **peer group** sits between 로컬 and 협업, containing **(a)** each attached peer-main's channel tab and **(b)** two monitors: `🔀 Peer↔Peer` (A2A between attached peer-mains) and `🔀 Peer↔Collab` (peer-main ↔ collab traffic). The main group gains a third monitor `🔀 Main↔Peer`, split out exactly as `🔀 Main↔Collab` was. **Monitor classification is peer-first**: any A2A pair involving a `peer` endpoint classifies to the peer-family monitors (peer+peer → Peer↔Peer; peer+collab → Peer↔Collab; peer+anything-else → Main↔Peer) before the legacy upstream/collab/board precedence runs. All monitors — the peer three and the legacy four alike — are **lazily materialized**: a monitor tab renders only once its conversation has content (first A2A push creates the channel); an empty monitor never occupies tab space.
- **Prompt-target selector (v2.4.52)** — the prompt-injection header row carries, at its right end, a compact selector that **always indicates the effective delivery target** (group-tinted dot + `optgroup`-per-group agent list). Selecting a tab or tab group immediately re-indicates the auto-resolved target (a group resolves to its representative worker); the operator MAY override the target for the current selection, and the override resets on the next tab/group switch. Monitor tabs stay read-only — the selector disables rather than making a monitor writable.
- **Slash-command autocomplete (v2.4.67)** — typing `/` at the start of the prompt-injection composer opens a candidate list that narrows as the token grows, mirroring a harness CLI palette: ↑/↓ move the selection, Enter/Tab apply it (token completed + trailing space; Ctrl+Enter still sends as-is), **ESC closes the candidate list only** (never the window — the keydown stops propagating so outer close handlers don't fire), and any whitespace ends the autocomplete session. Candidates are **manifest-first**: when the effective target (per the prompt-target selector) has declared a `CommandManifest`, its commands list first (선언-badged); targets without a declaration fall back to a deliberately conservative common set (공통-badged) whose descriptions state that interpretation belongs to the target harness — the board never fabricates harness-specific palettes it cannot verify. Room targets get no candidates (room utterances are free speech, §13.30). Manifest values are wire-derived untrusted input → rendered textContent-only per §8.1. **Token-based trigger (v2.4.69)**: the autocomplete session opens wherever the token before the cursor — the text after the last whitespace/newline — matches `/` + command charset (`[A-Za-z0-9_-]`), so a command typed mid-sentence after a space or newline completes too; the moment the token stops looking like a command and starts looking like a path (a second `/`, a dot, any non-command character — `src/foo`, `./x`, `/README.md`), the list closes itself. Apply replaces the token only, preserving surrounding text.
- **`CommandManifest` (v2.4.67, data-plane declaration)** — an agent MAY declare the slash commands it can **actually honor when they arrive as prompt text**: `CUSTOM`/`CommandManifest` with `value.commands[{name, desc}]` (`name` must start with `/`; the server caps count and field lengths). The server keeps a per-agent latest-wins registry persisted beside the channel-role store (`ws-history/.cmd-manifests.json`) and ships it to boards inside the History payload (`manifests` field), so candidates survive refresh, cold channels, and history trimming. Because the declaration is an ordinary data-plane event — not a bridge or protocol feature — **any harness adapter declares its palette the same way** (Claude Code, Codex, Hermes, OpenClaw alike). Declaration rule: only commands the receiving agent can honor on receipt — e.g. a Claude Code session declares its invocable skills, not host-CLI built-ins it cannot trigger itself; those generic verbs stay in the board-side fallback where their unverified nature is labeled.

#### 13.23.5 verify-nway backend axis (static drift detection)
The EG-ops `verify-nway-version.cjs` gains a backend axis: **(1)** the reference `backends.json` is schema-valid; **(2)** every declared `role` is one the dashboard actually renders (the `byRole` set) — a role nothing projects is drift; **(3)** where a deployment's instance + `local-keys/` both exist, every `connection: local` agent has a matching `local-keys/<id>.key` and every key file is declared — the static proxy for "who is actually a local worker", catching the swap-tracking gap deterministically.

#### 13.23.6 Cross-links
§13.1 role model · §13.9 collab-peer monitor split (the parallel for Main↔Board) · Superscalar §4 Andon (amber reservation). Reference impl: `constellation/reference/dashboard/{app.js, style.css, backends.json}`; axis: EG-ops `verify-nway-version.cjs`.

### 13.24 PWA (installable + offline shell) + board title customization

#### 13.24.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.27 (2026-06-13). The reference dashboard becomes an installable PWA, and the board title becomes a per-deployment value (the EG self-board sets it to "EstreGenesis"). C2-adjacent UX absorption; dashboard-side, with one small server addition (MIME).

#### 13.24.2 PWA — installable + offline shell (#3a)
- **`manifest.webmanifest`** — standalone display, theme/background color, icons (192/512, `any` + `maskable`). The deployment supplies its own icon (this board uses the EstreGenesis symbol, square-padded 8% for the maskable safe zone).
- **`sw.js`** (service worker) — app-shell **network-first** cache (dashboard updates land immediately; offline falls back to cache), live data (`/api`, `/ws`, `/join`) bypassed (never cached), `notificationclick` focuses the board window. Registered from `index.html`.
- **Server MIME** — the static server's MIME map gains `.webmanifest` (`application/manifest+json`) + `.png`; a board restart applies it (manifest must serve with the correct type for install).
- **Notifications** — **tier-1 shipped (v2.4.28)**: a 🔔 settings dropdown (master toggle + per-item toggles — 검토요청 / A2A 수신 / 작업 오류·중단) requests permission and fires `new Notification` on **live (non-replay)** events: a new unresolved decision (`renderDecisions` seen-set, first render suppressed), meaningful A2A (`a2acard` rows in `wsPushRow`), `RUN_ERROR`. Prefs persist to localStorage. **tier-2 shipped (v2.4.43 — Web Push, §13.24.4)**: VAPID + server-held subscriptions, fires while the PWA is fully closed. This is the "human-gate → OS" surface (Superscalar agent-time vs human-time — a notification shortens human-response latency).

#### 13.24.3 Board title customization (formal)
`backends.json` gains a **board-level `boardTitle`** field (default `"Constellation"`). At load the dashboard applies it to the topbar brand (`#board-name`) + the document title; `sync-dashboard` templates the *deployed* `manifest.webmanifest` `name`/`short_name` from it (so the PWA install name matches the deployment). Absent → `"Constellation"` default. EG self-board → `"EstreGenesis"`. This replaces the previously source-hardcoded title — the board identity is now deployment config, not a fork point.

#### 13.24.4 tier-2 Web Push (#3b — fires while the PWA is closed)
v2.4.43 (2026-06-20). tier-1 (§13.24.2) only fires while a board tab/SW is alive; tier-2 closes that gap — OS-level notifications delivered even when the dashboard is fully closed. Implemented **dependency-free** (node built-in `crypto`/`https` only — no `web-push` library):
- **VAPID keypair** — a P-256 (`prime256v1`) keypair self-generated via node `crypto`, persisted to `.vapid.json` (gitignored, per-deployment). The `applicationServerKey` handed to the browser is the uncompressed EC point (`0x04 || X || Y`, 65 bytes, base64url).
- **Signing** — the VAPID JWT is ES256 (ECDSA P-256 + SHA-256); the JWS signature is the raw `r || s` 64-byte form via `crypto.sign(…, { dsaEncoding: 'ieee-p1363' })`. `aud` = push-endpoint origin, `exp` ≤ 12h, `sub` = a `mailto:` contact.
- **tickle delivery** — a payload-less VAPID push (RFC 8291 payload encryption is *avoided*, which is precisely what removes the library dependency). On the `push` event the service worker fetches `GET /api/push/latest` for the body and calls `showNotification`. Expired subscriptions (HTTP 404/410) are pruned automatically.
- **Endpoints** (4, on the UI surface → subject to the §13.25 `ui` allowlist): `GET /api/push/vapid-public-key`, `POST /api/push/subscribe`, `POST /api/push/unsubscribe`, `GET /api/push/latest`.
- **Trigger** — every message crossing `wsToBoards` (the board-broadcast path that already carries A2A for dashboard observation) is filtered by a noise blocklist (Heartbeat / AgentList / Ack / OnboardAck / control kinds / non-CUSTOM run-and-stream frames); meaningful A2A intents (Report / Delegate / decision intents …) push. Title = `<agent> · <intent>`, body = the message's `re` / `summary` / `text`.
- **Subscribe UX** — the 🔔 panel gains a **백그라운드 알림** toggle that requests permission, subscribes via `PushManager.subscribe({ userVisibleOnly: true, applicationServerKey })`, and POSTs the subscription; the toggle reflects the live subscription state.

Web Push is **per-origin**: each board origin holds its own VAPID keypair + subscriptions, so a board self-sufficiently pushes its own activity with no cross-origin dependency. Two boards sharing the same endpoint/key convention could later federate cross-board notifications.

### 13.25 Surface-scoped access control (#5a — LAN-exposure allowlists)

#### 13.25.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.39 (2026-06-19). When the board is exposed beyond loopback (`WS_BIND` non-loopback — the secure-by-default opt-in of v2.4.11), the three reachable surfaces gate **independently** rather than under one blanket rule. Purely additive — with no `access.json` the runtime behaves exactly as before (all permitted; the v2.4.11 warning remains the only signal). The LAN bind itself is still the operator's explicit `WS_BIND` flip; this section governs only *who*, once bound, may reach *which* surface. **v2.4.41 (#5a-3)** extends it — the **agent** surface gains its own IP allowlist (symmetric with UI/MCP), the `/ws` gating moves to HELLO (where agent vs MCP is known) with an upgrade-time pre-check to avoid leaking board state to fully-blocked IPs, `requireKey` is enforced at HELLO (URL *or* HELLO key — fixing a v2.4.39 gap where only the URL key was seen), and allowlist entries accept **CIDR** ranges (`192.168.0.0/24`) as well as exact IPs. **v2.4.42 (#5a-4)** makes exposure dashboard-operable: a persisted **`expose`** field (the WS_BIND on/off) flipped via a loopback-only `POST /api/restart` that self-restarts the server (a deployment-provided `restart-self-board.ps1` re-launches it), with the settings-modal access editor surfaced as a distinct **save-gated block** (vs the real-time window-placement block).

#### 13.25.2 The three surfaces
One HTTP+WS port exposes three surfaces:
- **UI** — the dashboard (`public/`) + the board endpoints (`/api/state`, `/api/events`, `/api/feedback`). Browser-reached, **no key** → gated by an IP allowlist.
- **agent** — A2A WebSocket clients on `/ws`. Two independent layers: an **IP allowlist** (`agent.allowlist`, symmetric with UI/MCP) *and* an optional key requirement (`agent.requireKey`) that rejects unkeyed/invalid-key joins — closing the v2.4.11 unauthenticated-board vector (anyone on the LAN issuing keys / `SetMain`). Defence-in-depth: "only my known IPs **and** only with a key".
- **MCP** — the MCP-proxy WS client (§8), identified at HELLO by `capabilities` containing `'mcp-proxy'` → its own IP allowlist, **independent of UI and agent** (e.g. expose the dashboard to LAN phones while keeping MCP loopback-only).

All three IP allowlists accept exact IPs (IPv4/IPv6) and IPv4 CIDR ranges (`a.b.c.d/n`).

`/join/*` onboarding + the integration-doc whitelist are agent-facing and already key-gated, so they are **exempt** from the UI allowlist (IP-blocking them would break remote agent onboarding).

#### 13.25.3 `access.json` (server-side, gitignored)
A file beside `server.cjs` (`ACCESS_FILE` env relocates it), hot-reloaded via `fs.watchFile` (no restart):
```json
{ "expose": false, "ui": { "allowlist": null }, "agent": { "allowlist": null, "requireKey": false }, "mcp": { "allowlist": null } }
```
- `allowlist`: `null`/absent = **allow-all** (default); an array = only those entries — each an **exact IP** (IPv4/IPv6) or an **IPv4 CIDR** range (`a.b.c.d/n`; IPv6 CIDR not yet, exact IPv6 works). Loopback (`127.0.0.1` / `::1`, IPv4-mapped `::ffff:` normalized) is **always** allowed.
- `agent.requireKey`: when `true`, a `/ws` join from a non-loopback IP without a valid registered key (`wsValidKey`, resolved from the URL *or* the HELLO message) is closed at HELLO.
- `expose` (#5a-4): when `true`, the server binds `0.0.0.0` (LAN) instead of `127.0.0.1` **if the `WS_BIND` env is unset** (env always wins). A **bind-time** value — changing it takes effect only on restart (`/api/restart`), unlike the allowlists which hot-reload.
- **Fail-open by default**: a missing/corrupt file resets to the all-permissive default (incl. `expose:false`) — a security gate is an explicit opt-in, never an accidental lockout. On a loopback bind the IP gate is wholly inert (a local-only board needs no IP rules).

#### 13.25.4 Enforcement points
- **UI** — top of the HTTP handler, before routing (exempting `/join/*` + integration docs): non-allowed IP → `403`.
- **`/ws` upgrade pre-check** — agent and MCP share the `/ws` transport and are only distinguished at HELLO, yet the server emits board state (AgentList/History) right after the handshake. So at `upgrade`, an exposed-non-loopback IP blocked on **both** `agent` and `mcp` is `socket.destroy()`'d before any state is sent (leak prevention); an IP allowed on either passes through to HELLO.
- **agent / MCP** — at `HELLO` the surface is resolved (`mcp-proxy` capability → `mcp`, else `agent`) and that surface's IP allowlist is applied; then, if `requireKey`, the key (URL or HELLO) is checked. Either failure → `conn.close()` before the agent registers.

#### 13.25.5 `/api/access`
- `GET /api/access` → `{ ok, access, exposed, bind }` (behind the UI gate — only UI-allowed callers read it).
- `POST /api/access` → replaces the config (shape-validated, then `loadAccess()`). **Loopback-only** — the operator manages allowlists from the local machine; a remote caller (even a UI-allowed one) cannot rewrite the access policy.
- `POST /api/restart` (#5a-4) → **loopback-only** self-restart, to apply an `expose` change: spawns the deployment's `restart-self-board.ps1` (Windows: via `cmd /c start` for a true detach that survives the server's own exit — a plain detached spawn does not) then `process.exit`s; the script frees the port and re-launches `start-self-board.ps1`, the new process reading the new `expose`. Absent script / non-Windows → logged no-op (manual restart).

#### 13.25.6 Cross-links
- v2.4.11 secure-by-default bind — the opt-in this section refines.
- §3.1 KEY-MGMT — the keys the `agent` surface trusts.
- §8 MCP integration — the `mcp-proxy` client this gates.
- The dashboard access editor (settings-modal "접속 제어" section — a distinct **save-gated block** vs the real-time 창 배치 block): a **네트워크 노출 끄기/켜기** master toggle (`expose`; dims the IP policy when off), per-surface **기본 차단/허용** toggles for UI/agent/MCP each with a CIDR-capable allowlist textarea, a `requireKey` checkbox, an exposed/bind status badge, and an exposed-without-key warning. **저장** writes `access.json` (allowlists hot-reload); **저장 및 재시작** also `POST /api/restart`s to apply an `expose` change. Shipped v2.4.40 (#5a-2) → 3 surfaces + CIDR v2.4.41 (#5a-3) → expose toggle + self-restart + block separation v2.4.42 (#5a-4). Settings modal title generalized to "⚙ 설정".

#### 13.25.7 Multi-hat operator — hub operator = peer (small-team identity, v2.4.48)

In a small team the same human (and their agent) is often **both** the hub operator and a peer — e.g. the operator who runs the NAS hub over SSH is also an `upstream` peer on it. "Who issues the key, to whom" then converges on oneself, and the legitimacy of self-issuance was undefined.

- **Per-role-instance canonical-id (MUST)**: even under one operating human, the `hub-main` role (e.g. `nas-hub-main`) and the `peer-main` role (e.g. `estre-peer`) take **separate** canonical ids — they are distinct roles, not aliases, so the §13.9.2 alias-collapsing discipline does NOT apply to them.
- **Self-issuance is legitimate**: in an operator-is-peer deployment, self-issuing a `uk-` key is a normal procedure, not a smell. Record the issuance in board history or the backup repo (§13.28) for auditability (SHOULD).
- **The real trust boundary is the surface allowlist (§13.25) + the secret-storage location, not the key ceremony.** A small team SHOULD NOT defer adoption over key procedure — starting with `requireKey=false` on a loopback / LAN-trusted board is a valid posture; add keys when the exposure surface grows.

### 13.26 Echo-mode — mirroring an agent's local chat to the board (remote-control substrate)

An agent's *primary* interface is its own client (Claude Code, an IDE, a terminal) where a human converses with it directly. The board, by contrast, is a *shared observation + coordination* surface. **Echo-mode** bridges the two: when an agent's echo-mode is ON, its local human↔agent conversation is mirrored **bidirectionally** onto the board's real-time conversation channel, so a human watching the board can both *see* and *drive* that agent through the board. This turns Constellation into a **remote-control** surface for the agents on it.

Echo-mode is a per-agent mode, not a board-wide setting. It reuses the existing real-time conversation wire (§13.16.12) and dashboard rendering — it adds a *protocol discipline*, not a new transport. It has **three levels** (§13.26.4): **off**, **on** (turn-final conversation), and **mirror** (a live activity stream that also echoes progress and thinking, at the level of a chat-gateway bot).

#### 13.26.1 The two directions

- **Local → board (outbound mirror).** While echo-mode is enabled the agent mirrors onto its own board channel — *what* is mirrored depends on the **level** (§13.26.4):
  - the **human's local prompt** that opened the turn → a `UserPrompt` with `source:'user'` (both levels; so the board shows *both* sides of the conversation). *(A prompt that arrived **from** the board is already on the board — do not re-emit it; just quote it locally per the inbound rule below.)*
  - each **assistant turn's output** → a `TEXT_MESSAGE` (streaming `TEXT_MESSAGE_START`/`_CONTENT`/`_END` when available, else one complete `TEXT_MESSAGE`) — **both levels**.
  - **`mirror` level only** — a live activity stream *as the turn runs*: tool calls → `TOOL_CALL_START`/`_ARGS`/`_END`/`_RESULT` cards, step boundaries → `STEP_STARTED`/`_FINISHED`, run boundaries → `RUN_STARTED`/`_FINISHED`, and **thinking narration** → short `TEXT_MESSAGE`/`STEP` status lines ("analyzing X…", a turn-end thinking summary). Raw chain-of-thought is not streamed verbatim (too verbose, and no host thinking-hook exists); the mirror level emits *progress + narration + summary*, which is the chat-gateway (e.g. Telegram-bot) echo level.
- **Board → local (inbound drive).** A human typing into the board's real-time window for this agent emits a `UserPrompt` (dashboard `wsSend`, §13.16.12) that reaches the agent's inbox (§13.16). On receipt the agent **MUST first echo the received prompt back into its local chat as a quoted line** (`> board: <text>`) and *then* act on it — so the local transcript stays a faithful, self-contained record even when the driving input arrived out-of-band. Inbound drive works at every enabled level (`on` and `mirror`).

#### 13.26.2 Structured-choice reconciliation (the §13.17 tension)

§13.17 forbids blocking structured-choice prompts in the main chat (they must route to the board). Echo-mode makes this a hard constraint rather than a guideline, because a blocking selection UI in the local chat would **hold the turn** and defeat remote-control (the human at the board could never advance it). Therefore, while echo-mode is ON, an agent facing a decision:

1. In the **local chat**, renders the options as **plain text** (`1/2/3` or `a/b/c` + a one-line each) and accepts a **free-form prompt** — never a blocking selection widget. The turn does not hold on a local UI.
2. On the **board**, emits a `SelectionPrompt` (§13.16.12 #406 UI6) so the real-time window shows the rich chip-card UI.
3. Resolves on **either** path: a board answer (`SelectionAnswer` → `SelectionResolved`) *or* the human typing the option token as a local/board `UserPrompt`. First resolution wins; the other surface is dimmed (`SelectionResolved`).

This is the same "one decision, two faithful surfaces" property as §13.17, generalized to the echo-mirror.

#### 13.26.3 Default by provenance (who joined whom)

Echo-mode's value is *giving a human a channel to an agent they otherwise cannot reach*. So the default follows **join provenance**:

| How the agent joined | Default echo-mode | Why |
|---|:-:|---|
| **Human-joined** (a person issued its key / started it) | **OFF** | The human already has a direct channel (that agent's own client). Mirroring is redundant and noisy — opt in only when remote-control is wanted. |
| **Agent-spawned** (another agent called/spawned it — e.g. a board-observer via `join-local.cjs`, a sub-worker) | **ON** | The human has **no** direct client for this agent; the board is the *only* place they can see or drive it. Echo-mode makes it reachable. |

The default is **per-agent overridable** by the user (`/echo-mode on|off <agentId>`), and a human-issued explicit instruction always wins over the provenance default.

#### 13.26.4 Levels + toggle

Echo-mode is a **three-level** per-agent setting:

| Level | Mirrors (local → board) | Use |
|---|---|---|
| **off** | nothing | Default for human-joined agents (§13.26.3). |
| **on** | the human's prompt + the assistant's **turn-final text** + selection prompts | Conversation echo — a human at the board sees the exchange and can drive it, without the tool-by-tool noise. |
| **mirror** | everything in `on` **+ live progress** (tool calls, steps, run boundaries) **+ thinking narration/summary**, streamed *as the turn runs* | Chat-gateway-level echo (Telegram-bot feel) — the board shows *what the agent is doing right now*, not just the final answer. |

- **`/echo-mode off|on|mirror|status [agentId]`** (skill, §13.26.6) is the control surface. With no `agentId` it targets the invoking agent; with one it targets that agent (main-authority gated, like other cross-agent controls). Board→local *inbound drive* works at both `on` and `mirror`; only the *outbound* richness differs.
- **State** is a per-agent level the agent reads to decide what to mirror, and announces to the board so the dashboard can badge the agent and treat its channel as a live conversation. Reference: a local `.echo-mode` marker keyed by `agentId` (`{ level, provenance }`) for the agent's own runtime + an `EchoModeState { agentId, level, provenance }` CUSTOM announced on change (idempotent; the board badges the agent and, when enabled, renders its channel as the primary conversation rather than a monitor lane).

#### 13.26.5 Granularity by level + exposure (honest constraints)

- **Granularity is per level, and neither level is token-streaming.** `on` is **turn-granular**: the board receives the agent's *complete* turn text at turn-end (one `TEXT_MESSAGE`), via the Stop hook. `mirror` is **action-granular**: tool calls and steps stream to the board *as they happen* (PostToolUse hook, one emit per tool call) so the board tracks live progress — but the text *within* a single message is still not streamed keystroke-by-keystroke (no host token-streaming hook exists). An agent that *can* stream natively MAY use `TEXT_MESSAGE_START/_CONTENT/_END` for a finer feel.
- **Exposure is disclosure.** Echo-mode copies the local chat onto the board, so the board's access surface (§13.25 #5a) governs *who* can now read that conversation. Mirroring to a network-exposed board is a disclosure event — echo-mode MUST respect §13.14 redaction on what it emits, and SHOULD warn (or refuse) when the target board is exposed beyond loopback/allowlist. Remote-control convenience never overrides the access gate.

#### 13.26.6 Mechanization (reference) + cross-links

- **Reference emit — level-tiered hooks.** `echo-emit.cjs` reads the agent's `.echo-mode` level (keyed by `agentId`) and emits accordingly:
  - **`on`** — a **Stop** hook extracts the last assistant turn from the session transcript and emits it as `TEXT_MESSAGE` on the agent's board channel; a local opening prompt → `UserPrompt{source:'user'}`.
  - **`mirror`** — additionally a **PostToolUse** hook emits each tool call as `TOOL_CALL_*` cards *as it completes* (live progress); a **PreToolUse** hook MAY emit a `STEP`/status line ("running X…"); the Stop hook also appends a short **thinking summary** distilled from the turn's thinking blocks; `RUN_STARTED`/`_FINISHED` bracket the turn.
  - All emit hooks are **level-gated**: no-op at `off`, and the `mirror`-only tiers (PreToolUse/PostToolUse, thinking summary) are skipped at `on`.
- **Emit formatting (board-legibility).** Mirrored text lands in the board's conversation stream, so format for that target: put **sequenced/numbered items each on their own line** (one `①`/`1.` item per line, never an inline run-on), and prefer short lines. A render-target formatting rule, not a content rule.
- **Provenance default + state announce (reference, v2.4.58).** `join-local.cjs` — the agent-spawned join path — seeds the `.echo-mode` marker with `{ level:'on', provenance:'agent-spawned' }` when the joining agent has no entry, and never overwrites an existing entry (explicit toggles included — §13.26.3's explicit-wins rule mechanized). On every (re)connect it (re)announces `EchoModeState` as an untargeted broadcast (idempotent; not a commitment-ack target, so no redelivery noise). The reference dashboard consumes the announce as a per-tab echo badge (`on` plain / `mirror` highlighted) — the "board badges the agent" half of §13.26.4.
- **Workflow-run mirror + floating inspector (reference, v2.4.61).** A deployment MAY run a watcher that mirrors multi-agent workflow runs onto the agent's channel: coalesced `STEP_*` lines (🧵-prefixed, one per poll tick at most) carrying a `wfRunId` field, plus a `WorkflowStatus` CUSTOM snapshot (`{runId, name, status, started, done, phases[], agents[{id, label?, state, preview?}], totalTokens?, durationMs?, logsTail?}`, throttled ≥10s per run). The reference dashboard consumes both: 🧵 STEP rows become clickable and open a **floating inspector** (draggable header, horizontal resize, content-height body, collapse + close) that live-renders the latest snapshot; history replay re-hydrates it, so completed runs stay inspectable. v2.4.63 widens the inspector into an **agent-activity monitor**: a second `SubagentStatus` snapshot (`{agents[{id, lastActivityS, sizeKB, state}], count}` — standalone subagent transcripts active within a 10-minute window, chosen because a measured agent composing one large tool call went 6+ minutes without a transcript flush) renders as its own section, a fixed 🧵 fab toggles the layer without needing a STEP row, and the window styles from the dashboard's real theme tokens so it follows light/dark mode (the v2.4.61 styling had pinned itself to dark fallbacks of nonexistent variables). Measured constraint that shaped the design: the harness's run-state file is a completion-time artifact — live progress must come from the run's journal, with the state file as the terminal enrichment (labels, tokens, duration).
- **Behavioral fallback**: absent the hooks, the `/echo-mode` skill defines the same protocol as an agent behavior (emit turn output + progress + quote board prompts explicitly) — the skill is the SSoT for the discipline; the hooks are the mechanization.
- **Cross-links**: §13.17 (main-chat structured-choice → board; echo-mode is its remote-control generalization) · §13.16 / §13.16.12 (inbox + dashboard conversation render this reuses) · §13.16.12 #406 UI6 `SelectionPrompt` (the choice UI) · §13.25 #5a (access surface governing the mirror's audience) · §13.14 (redaction on emitted content).

### 13.27 Headless hub-main — autonomous reasoning loop (no human session)

#### 13.27.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.48 (2026-07-09). Distilled from a downstream-adapter dogfood (a NAS headless container curating a multi-project board, verified end-to-end). §4 runtime patterns assume a human session behind a turn-based agent; §3's autopilot is an in-session mode. **A board main that resides with no human session at all** — the `hub-main` duty profile of §13.9.3 — had no pattern in the spec or the reference runtime. This section is the pattern; the reference scripts are upstream candidates (§13.27.3).

#### 13.27.2 Invariants
A headless hub-main is a **supervisor loop** that spawns a one-shot reasoning process (a `claude -p`-style headless invocation) per wake. The loop MUST satisfy:

1. **Wake economy (event-driven MUST)** — the loop reasons only on an inbox change that passes the §13.16.9 meaningful filter (the A2A-intent group). Idle-heartbeat reasoning is forbidden (the loop form of the no-idle-chatter rule). A watcher blocks until a meaningful change (reference: `self-wake-watcher.sh` with `WS_STANDBY_MODE=always`, §13.16.6).
2. **Cursor discipline (at-least-once MUST)** — a reasoning turn that fails (abnormal exit / timeout) MUST NOT advance the inbox cursor; the next wake idempotently re-processes the same span. The cursor advances **only on success**. This extends §13.13.2's receiver-side at-least-once up into the agent (reasoning) layer.
3. **Noise absorption (SHOULD)** — if every new line is in a noise group, advance the cursor without spawning a reasoning process (a second check downstream of the watcher filter — defence against filter drift).
4. **Security boundary (SHOULD)** — the reasoning process runs in a cwd from which secret directories are unreachable, with a minimal tool allowlist (file R/W only, no shell). The board + doc stores are the only explicitly-granted extra paths.
5. **Turn timeout (MUST)** — a wall-clock ceiling per turn (reference value 900s); on hang the supervisor reclaims the process.
6. **Model routing (§13.16.9 `tier` consumer)** — because each wake is a separate process, the `tier`→model+effort mapping is free: a hub-main SHOULD route `routine` intents to a low-cost model / low effort and `escalation` intents to a high-capability model / high effort. Grounding (dogfood): bookkeeping is intelligence-insensitive, and for a resident agent the token/quota economy is the dominant variable.

#### 13.27.3 Reference runtime — `constellation/reference/runtime/hub-main/` (v2.4.49, upstreamed)
The adopter's verified implementation was contributed under §13.14 redaction and now ships in-repo at **`constellation/reference/runtime/hub-main/`** (generalization substitution points in its README):
- `hub-loop.sh` — supervisor: watcher(block, `WS_STANDBY_MODE=always`) → turn → backup, looping; echoes dependency paths at startup; initializes the cursor to the current line count on first start (no past-noise re-processing).
- `hub-turn.sh` — ① pull the doc repo (best-effort, `GIT_ASKPASS`) → ② classify inbox-since-cursor in one node pass (noise absorb / `tier` decide — the lists mirror the §13.16.9 4-group + tier SSoT, lockstep-updated; unclassified non-noise fail-safes to `escalation`) → ③ `tier`→model+effort one-shot with a minimal tool allowlist + `add-dir` + 900s timeout → ④ advance the cursor **only on success**.
- `hub-backup.sh` — on change: add → secret gate (§13.28.3) → commit → push; a push failure keeps the local commit and retries next tick (offline tolerance).

Companion artifacts (same directory): `git-askpass.sh` (§13.28.5 headless git auth), `Dockerfile` baking stable deps (restart tolerance), and the hub-main charter `CLAUDE.md.template` (§13.9.3). The loop reuses the parent `runtime/self-wake-watcher.sh` as its blocking watcher.

#### 13.27.4 The loop contract — implementation-independent statement (v2.4.56)
§13.27.2's invariants were written against one runtime shape (`claude -p` one-shots under a bash supervisor). Restated as an **implementation-independent contract**, so any runtime that owns its own agent loop — a local-LLM personal-AI environment, a provider-native scheduler, an embedded worker — can be a conforming EG loop without resembling the reference scripts. A conforming loop provides **five elements**:

1. **Wake sources** — a declared, enumerable set of change feeds (inbox file, WS push, queue) with a meaningful-filter at the boundary (§13.16.9 SSoT). No polling-as-reasoning; no idle wakes. *Room traffic composes here*: §13.30 room messages wake a worker-class participant only on `Delegate` or explicit `addressee` naming (the D1 silence default, enforced at the filter — dogfood-measured 2026-07-18).
2. **At-least-once consumption** — a durable cursor per feed; advance **only on turn success**; failed turns re-process idempotently. Consumers therefore MUST be id-idempotent (the charter carries this duty).
3. **A charter** — the per-wake process receives a written role contract (scope, autonomy boundary, file contracts, reply obligations, machine-count rules). The charter is an artifact, versioned with the deployment — never implicit prompt memory.
4. **Model routing** — the `tier`→model+effort mapping of §13.27.2-6, generalized: the loop MAY route each wake to any model the operator owns (including local models); the contract only requires that `escalation`-tier intents never route below the deployment's declared capability floor.
5. **Safety boundary** — per-wake tool/path allowlists + wall-clock ceiling + supervisor reclaim. The loop, not the model, owns termination.

Standing idle duty (v2.4.59): a resident loop that owns a board SHOULD spend idle capacity on the §13.31.4-⑥ sweep cadence — when board-update traffic has been silent for the idle window while work signals continue, the next tick runs the retrospective sweep (the boardsweep skill) instead of sleeping.

Conformance today: the reference `hub-main/` scripts (§13.27.3) and the EG-ops `observer-loop`/`observer-turn` pair are the two measured implementations; a §13.30-aware wake filter is part of both since 2026-07-18. Composition: a host that implements this contract *and* the kit's Harness Adapter Contract (`plugins/HARNESS-ADAPTER-CONTRACT.md`, Stage 3) runs EG disciplines unattended on its own loop — the two contracts deliberately partition "when the agent runs" (here) from "what it runs with" (adapter).

### 13.28 Board persistence & backup contract

#### 13.28.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.48 (2026-07-09, downstream-adapter dogfood). The board `state.json` is the SSoT, yet lives as a single file on a single machine, and the spec had no durable-backup contract (§13.25.3 only notes `access.json` is gitignored). Version-controlling the deployment directory is the natural backup — but doing it naively staged secrets. This section is the contract that makes board backup safe.

#### 13.28.2 Tracked vs transient classification
- **tracked** — `state.json` · runtime code · dashboard static assets · (with care) `access.json` *only if it carries no key material*.
- **transient (MUST NOT track)** — the transport queues (`inbox` / `outbox` / `feedback`), cursors, locks, `ws-history/`, logs, the agent-credential cache `HOME`, and binary-prefixed files. **Tracking a transport queue permanently records A2A message bodies** — a secret / PII exposure surface, so transient is MUST here.

#### 13.28.3 Secret gate (MUST)
Before each commit, scan the staged content for real-token structural patterns and, on a hit, unstage + abort the push. Patterns are tightened to **real-token structure** so the gate script's own pattern literals do not self-match (observed failure: a gate whose literal `sk-ant-oat` string matched itself → a backup ABORT loop): e.g. `sk-ant-oat01-[A-Za-z0-9_-]{20,}`, `ghp_[A-Za-z0-9]{20,}`, `-----BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY-----`. Tightening beats excluding the gate from tracking — the gate itself is worth versioning.

#### 13.28.4 `.gitignore` contract
Comments on their **own line only** (git parses a trailing/inline comment as part of the pattern) and **LF-enforced** (CRLF turns every pattern into `pattern\r`, silently disabling all matching → secret staging; the two real incidents behind this section). Ship a reference `.gitignore` + a `.gitattributes` (scripts `eol=lf`; cf. `constellation/reference/runtime/.gitattributes`).

#### 13.28.5 Backup trigger + headless auth
The hub-main loop's turn-end hook (or a state-write hook) drives the backup; the commit message carries a snapshot timestamp; a push failure keeps the local commit and retries next tick (offline tolerance). Headless git auth SHOULD use a `GIT_ASKPASS` helper that references the PAT from env only (no plaintext credential file on disk — important when `HOME` sits inside the backed-up directory): the helper file itself is not a secret and is trackable, unlike `credential.helper store`'s plaintext output.

### 13.29 Ownership registry & claim layering (conflict prevention)

#### 13.29.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.48 (2026-07-09, downstream-adapter dogfood). §13.19 (deadlock) / §13.20 (blocker) / §13.22 (cross-repo PR) are *post-conflict* protocols. In multi-repo orchestration (an overview doc repo + N code repos + per-peer ownership splits) the actual first line of defence against conflict was a **static ownership registry** (the adopter's `AGENTS.md` ownership table). The protocol did not know about it, so a hub-main had no board data to detect "two peers reporting the same unit."

#### 13.29.2 Registry contract
The board `state.json` gains an optional `ownership: [{ unit, owner (canonical-id), repo?, note? }]` field — the hub-main mirrors the owning doc's ownership table (the SSoT is the doc; the board field is a **projection**). This makes ownership comparable against the `unit` field of a peer's `WorkerReport` (the §13.16.9 recommended payload, added same cut).

#### 13.29.3 Claim layering (3 layers)
① **static ownership** (registry — the default boundary) → ② **durable claim** (a git file, for cross-cutting files — valid even offline) → ③ **live claim** (A2A `HandoffRequested` / `Handoff` — immediate cross-session coordination). Rule: *a lower layer's claim MUST NOT contradict a higher layer; cross-unit work takes ② first and notifies via ③.*

#### 13.29.4 Violation surfacing (SHOULD)
A hub-main (coordination duty) that detects an out-of-ownership report by registry comparison SHOULD surface it on the `decisions` track — **not** auto-block (the ownership table itself may be provisional; a human adjudicates).

#### 13.29.5 Contract-transition intent (candidate)
A new A2A intent under evaluation — `ContractUpdate { contract, from, to, refs }` (tier `escalation`) — to announce an interface-contract (`_contracts`-class) DRAFT → REVIEW → ACTIVE transition. It becomes the trigger signal for N-way surface sync when one feature spans multiple repo surfaces.

### 13.30 Roundtable — multi-party topic rooms (3+ participants)

#### 13.30.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.53 (2026-07-17). Everything before this section is 1:1 — a targeted message, one sender, one receiver. That shape does not scale to three or more speakers: a two-agent messenger-group dogfood produced an **echo storm** (both agents answering every human message, then answering each other's answers), the same announcement had to be delivered N times over N 1:1 channels, and per-pair threads fragmented the shared context so that one side went stale without knowing. A 5-axis deep research pass (121 sources, 12 adversarially verified claims) converged on one structure across frameworks, chat-protocol standards, and incident history: a **two-layer split** — deterministic floor control belongs to the protocol, probabilistic speech judgment belongs to agent discipline. LLMs are measurably weaker at *when to speak* than at *what to say*, so every surveyed framework pairs model judgment with hard structural guards; conversely, purely structural allocation (equalized-random turns) demonstrably breaks adjacency pairs, and the semantic echo class (mutual-confirmation spirals) is invisible to string/ID-level machinery — only discipline catches it. The protocol floor is therefore designed as *"a bottom that keeps an ill-disciplined participant from breaking the room"*, not as a scheduler that speaks for well-behaved ones.

#### 13.30.2 The room object
A board MAY host any number of rooms. `{ roomId, topic, mode: 'persistent'|'temporary', moderated: bool, participants: [{ agentId, role: 'moderator'|'participant'|'observer', voice: bool, speakerClass: 'human-operator'|'agent' }], floor: { holder?, queue[] }, budgets: { maxConsecutive, ratePerMin, maxAutoHop, stallRounds }, artifacts: { header, decisions[], summary }, createdBy, createdAt, closedAt? }`. A `temporary` room dissolves on explicit close or when its purpose is declared met (MUC-lineage `temporary` semantics); `persistent` rooms survive restarts. `role` is session-scoped standing *in this room*; it is deliberately distinct from board-level standing (the MUC role-vs-affiliation split).

#### 13.30.3 Envelope extensions
A room message is a normal CUSTOM envelope (msgId, ack tiers, dedup — all §13.13 machinery inherited) plus: **`roomId`** · **`addressee[]`** (explicit naming — marks a response *obligation* on the named participants; the adjacency-pair anchor) · **`replyTo`** (msgId of the first pair part being answered) · **`floorIntent`** (`request` | `release` | `yield`, optionally with a scalar importance bid) · **`authority`** (`directive` | `proposal` | `info` — an agent-authored instruction-shaped utterance is demoted to `proposal` by default; promotion to binding requires a human ack or a pre-delegated scope) · **`notice`** (bool — "automated output, MUST NOT be auto-replied to"; the Matrix `m.notice` rule as a message class; watcher guidance: the recommended default is **non-wake** for turn-based participants unless the receiver is in `addressee[]` — keeps room traffic aligned with the §13.16.9 wake economy) · **`autoHop`** (server-maintained depth of the agent-reply chain since the last human utterance).

#### 13.30.4 Server-enforced floor (deterministic bottom)
1. **Fan-out** — a room message is relayed to every participant over the existing 1:1 targeted path (at-least-once + commitment ack inherited unchanged). *Announce once, reach all.* Turn-spawned local workers (a supervisor that spawns a model turn per inbound — §13.27 lineage) MUST NOT treat every fan-out copy as a wake trigger: wake only on delegation-class work or when named in `addressee[]`, cursor-advance otherwise (first-day dogfood: a scribe worker woke once per room utterance and spent whole turns reporting "not applicable").
2. **autoHop cap** — when `autoHop ≥ budgets.maxAutoHop`, further agent replies in that chain are **parked** and a `RoomStall` event is emitted. Never a silent drop: silence-by-fallback is the documented failure smell of LLM speaker selection. The default cap sits **above** the conduct layer's self-cap (D4: 3-5) with margin — default `maxAutoHop: 6` — so a discipline-compliant participant never hits the floor first (the floor is a bottom for the ill-disciplined, not a ceiling on the compliant). Parking is record-only, no auto-release: the resume path is a human/moderator utterance resetting the chain, after which the parked sender MAY re-send — re-gated through D1 (only if the message is still worth saying).
3. **Rate + consecutive caps** — per-agent per-room rate limit, and a cap on consecutive utterances by the same speaker (the generalization of `allow_repeat_speaker`).
4. **Stall detection** — N rounds with no new addressee and no new decision → `RoomStall` → escalate to the moderator (if any) or the human.
5. **Human priority** — a `human-operator` utterance broadcasts a **soft-yield** event: agents finish the turn in flight, then MUST incorporate the human utterance before starting a new one (the text-domain form of barge-in-yields). Humans are exempt from rate/voice constraints.
6. **Floor state single source of truth** — the server owns `floor` (BFCP lineage). In v1 it is *advisory*: naming and self-selection discipline drive who speaks; the server only tie-breaks concurrent `floorIntent: request` bids and guards against starvation. Hard floor assignment is deliberately NOT in v1.
7. **Notice-class surfacing** — an agent auto-reply to a `notice` message is surfaced as a warning event (visible discipline violation), not blocked.

#### 13.30.5 Room artifacts (shared context beyond the log)
Three pinned artifacts, per the ledger/blackboard lineage: **header** (room objective + currently-valid plan + role boundaries + **per-participant expected-latency declarations** — e.g. `latency: turn-based ~50min` — so a turn-based peer's pace is a declared property, not a discipline violation; versioned — a change emits an invalidation event, not a re-broadcast of the full text) · **`decisions[]`** (append-only with `supersedes` links; "currently valid" is always HEAD) · **`summary`** (running digest with an explicit `covers_until` message cursor — before the cursor the digest speaks, after it the raw tail does; re-based from the raw log periodically to cap summary drift). A room announcement replaces N 1:1 deliveries only when all four hold: the content is a **single canonical artifact with a version id**; recipients have a **consumption duty** (turn-start probe); confirmation is **ack-by-reference** (quoting the version id, unconfirmed recipients tracked); changes propagate as **invalidation + delta**. Individual delegations still restate a one-line anchor plus the pointer (the deliberate-redundancy safety net). Artifact fetch contract: `RequestRoomArtifacts { roomId }` → `RoomArtifacts { roomId, artifacts, version }` reply, plus the same event broadcast on change (invalidation + delta) — WS-only, symmetric with `RequestChannelHistory`. The write path is `RoomArtifactsUpdate { roomId, header? {text}, decision? {text, supersedes?}, summary? {text, covers_until} }` — participants and the board only; the server stamps editor/timestamp/per-artifact versions, appends decisions (`rd-<n>`, never rewritten), and broadcasts the delta under a single monotonically increasing artifacts `version` (the ack-by-reference target). Digest upkeep is naturally a scribe-worker duty (§13.23): the room owner delegates a summary refresh, the scribe reads the room channel tail and submits `RoomArtifactsUpdate { summary }` with an honest `covers_until` cursor.

#### 13.30.6 Conduct discipline (the agent-owned layer)
Normative procedure lives in the **`/roundtable` skill** (constellation plugin); the protocol only summarizes the nine duties so adopters know what the floor assumes: ① silence is the default output (respond-or-not is a separate decision made *before* content generation) ② being named in `addressee[]` creates a response obligation — answer or explicitly yield ③ unsolicited speech goes through `floorIntent: request` with an honest importance bid ④ agent↔agent exchanges self-cap (3-5 turns) without human input, then pause with a one-line state summary ⑤ late joiners and turn-based participants re-hydrate in fixed order — header → valid decisions → summary → raw tail after `covers_until`; never a full replay ⑥ announcements are consumed via ack-by-reference ⑦ closing is a structured field, not a magic string ⑧ a human utterance is a soft-yield event ⑨ the moderator hat, when assigned, holds procedure authority only (agenda, timebox, periodic summarization, participation management, decision capture) — never content authority.

Wake-path note (dogfooded): a turn-based participant SHOULD dual-path its wake source — a short-interval poll watcher plus an independent long-period fallback. A single pipeline watcher is one buffering bug away from silent deafness: in the first room dogfood, a mid-pipeline filter stage without per-line flushing trapped events in a 4 KiB block buffer, and the room looked idle to that participant while traffic flowed.

#### 13.30.7 Vocabulary & compatibility
Naming is deliberately aligned to the MUC/Matrix lineage — `voice`, `moderated`, `moderator`, `notice`, `temporary` — because the concept vocabulary is the longest-lived layer of this section. A2A compatibility guard: the room correlation key is an opaque string, never coupled 1:1 to an A2A `contextId` (a room may span many); room participation remains expressible as "N 1:1 sessions + server fan-out", so if the A2A ecosystem later standardizes a group extension, a room server becomes its host rather than its competitor.

#### 13.30.8 Dashboard projection
The prompt-target selector (§13.23.4) gains a **"➕ roundtable"** entry: topic input + multi-select of targets (group toggles included) + persistent/temporary choice → creates the room and a tab under a **roundtable tab group** (lazy-materialized like all A2A tabs). The tab renders the conversation plus collapsible pinned header/digest and participant chips (🎤 voice · 🪄 moderator · 👤 human). It is a *sending* surface (input enabled, target = the room), unlike read-only monitors. Room utterances are excluded from echo-mode (§13.26) mirroring — an agent's contribution to a room goes through the D1 gate only, never as an automatic mirror.

### 13.31 Board state schema — the data contract behind the dashboard

#### 13.31.1 Status & provenance
v2.4.57 (2026-07-18). The live-board state document has driven the dashboard since the board's first cut, but its field contract existed only as renderer code. An adopter measured the cost: a stage list written as `{name, state}` against the renderer's `{label, status}` contract survived two hygiene sweeps while rendering every stage as pending — render fallbacks silently swallow near-miss schemas (the consumer-contract lesson; see the boardsweep skill's schema-normalization clause). A second field observation: agents across adopting projects barely used the stage timeline at all — the feature was undiscoverable (absent from worker charters and from any spec surface) and the incentive misaligned (mid-work updates read as pure cost). This section makes the contract canonical and pairs it with a usage discipline.

#### 13.31.2 The state document
Top-level keys of the board state document (server-watched, live-rebroadcast on change): `projects[]` `{id, name, color}` — the group registry every entry's `project` references · `modes` (board-scoped operating policy: language, tone, pace, routing) · `freeRequest` (standing operator request) · `current[]` · `done[]` (newest-first) · `planned[]` · `decisions[]`. Common entry fields: `id` (the idempotency key for worker-applied updates — REQUIRED on anything a delegation may touch twice) · `project` (∈ `projects[].id`) · `title` (REQUIRED) · `when` (date) / `at` (ISO timestamp) · `detail` · `commit` / `ref` (VCS anchors — the retrospective sweep verifies them against the repository). `planned[]` adds: `priority` (ascending sort, absent = lowest) · `blocked` + `blockReason` + `unblock` · `waiting` (autonomous wait vs actionable now). `decisions[]` adds: `status` (`'open'` | `'resolved'`) · `kind` · `question` · `options[]` · `recommend` · `reviewedText` + `reviewedAt` (the resolution record; `detail` is plain text with `\n` line breaks, rendered escaped).

#### 13.31.3 Stage timelines (`current[]`)
A `current[]` entry MAY carry a staged progress shape: `stages: [{ label, status: 'pending' | 'active' | 'done' }]` — exactly these key names and status values. The renderer treats any unknown status as `pending`: fallback-not-error is deliberate forward compatibility, but it is also precisely why near-miss schemas fail silently — validate against **this** contract, not against plausibility. Optional companions: `sub[]` (sub-items, each MAY carry its own mini `stages`) and `blockedBy` (a `sub` index or a sub `id`; when it matches an existing sub-item the renderer draws the blocker link, and dangling references are ignored). The `active` stage's label doubles as the entry's one-line progress summary.

#### 13.31.4 Usage discipline
The schema only pays when entries actually use it: ① a multi-stage track (roughly 3+ distinguishable phases, or work spanning sessions or external waits) SHOULD be registered on `current[]` **with** `stages` at start — the scheduling round's "start it now" step is the natural hook; ② status transitions happen at stage boundaries only (entering or finishing a phase), never per-action — keeping the update cost near zero is what makes the discipline sustainable; ③ on completion the entry moves to `done[]`, where the `commit`/`ref` anchor is the durable evidence (carrying the final stage list is optional); ④ worker charters that apply board updates MUST carry this schema — `stages` included — so delegations can express it; a charter without the field is exactly how the contract stayed undiscoverable; ⑤ the retrospective sweep checks `stages` claims like any other board claim — an `active` stage on an abandoned track is drift; ⑥ **sweep cadence** — the retrospective pass runs **work-denominated, not wall-clock** (drift accumulates with off-board work, not with time): (a) **at session resume** — after a context compaction or workspace restart, before new board-relevant work; the post-compaction window is the highest-misregistration window on record (a measured resume-time sweep surfaced 12 record corrections, including identifier ghosts that had survived 40+ cuts), and quick scope (recent `done[]` + everything open on `current`/`planned`/`decisions`) suffices unless it surfaces anomalies; (b) **every ~5 release cuts or 7 days, whichever comes first** — full scope, resolving every recorded identifier against the repository; only the full pass catches slow corruption (lost tags, rewritten-away commits); (c) **on the idle signature** (resident boards — headless hub-mains, peer-run boards): board-update traffic silent for a window (suggest 24h) *while* work signals (commits, A2A traffic) continue — silence plus ongoing work is the drift signature, silence with no work needs no sweep; the §13.27 loop's idle tick is the natural executor; (d) **immediately after history-shape operations** — tag moves, history rewrites, force pushes — the class that mints unresolvable identifiers.

#### 13.31.5 Cross-links
§13.16.6 (watcher/cycle discipline the scheduling round composes with) · §13.20 (blocker manifest — `blockedBy` is its `current[]`-local cousin) · §13.23 (board-worker projection — the charter is the enforcement point) · the boardsweep skill (consumer-contract normalization) and the roundnext skill (start-with-stages hook).
